ما الذي أهون اللانتان را النقية الصحيحة عن الكون والحياة والتزام مقتضياتها
يظل بعض الناس ، ممن لم تتهيأ لديهم ثقافـة إسـلامـيـة كافيـة يتساءل : ما وجه الحاجة أو الضرورة الى أن يتعبدنا الله ) على فرض وجوده ( بهذا الدين ويلزمنا بكل هذا الذي يتضمنه من اعتقاد وعبادة وأحكام ؟ وهلاً يترك هذا الإله عباده أحراراً يقيمون حياتهم على الوجه الذي يريدون ، وينظمونها حسب الشكل أو الطريقة التي يحبون ؟.. وقد تمتد ببعضهم سلسلة هذا التساؤل فيسأل في ضيق وتعجب : وما حاجة الله في أن أحبس نفسي على عبادته العمر كله ، ومـا الـذي ينقصه أو يضره لولم أفعل ذلك(۱)

الإنسان مجهز بأخطر الصفات والملكات :
فكان أن جهز هذا المخلوق بمجموعة من الملكات والصفات ، لابد منها ، لتتكامل لديه القدرة على إدارة شأن هذا الكون وتعميره واستخدامه فبث فيـه صفة العقل وما يتفرع عنها من العلم والإدراك والقدرة على تحليل الأشياء وسبر أغوارها والوصول إلى ما وراءها ، وبث فيه معنى الأنانية ، وما يتفرع عنها من النزوع إلى الأثرة والتملك ، وبث فيه أسباب القوة ومقومات التدبير ، وما يتفرع عنهما من النزوع إلى السيطرة والعظمة والجاه ، ثم بث فيه مجموعة من العواطف والأشواق والانفعالات تعدّ متممة لقيمة تلك الصفات وفوائدها ، كالحب والكراهية والغضب وما إلى ذلك

إلا أن لهذه الصفات شرةً كبيرة ولها آفات عظام ، وهي أسلحة ذات حدين إن استعمل أحدهما جاء بالتنظيم العظيم للكون وبالخير الوفير للإنسان ، وإن استعمل الآخر أو استعملا معاً جاء ذلك بالشر الوبيل والفوضى الهائلة وأورث الإنسانية شقاء لا آخر له .
Secondly. What is the easier of the two pure correct [؟] about the universe and life and adherence to its requirements? Some people, who do not have sufficient Islamic culture, continue to ask: What is the need or necessity for God (assuming His existence) to obligate us with this religion and impose upon us all that it contains of belief, worship, and rulings? And why does this God not leave His servants free to establish their lives in the way they want, and organize them according to the form or method they prefer? And this chain of questioning may extend for some of them, so they ask in distress and astonishment: What need does God have for me to confine myself to worshipping Him all my life? And what does He lack or what would harm Him if I did not do that? (1) And it is necessary to have a sufficient and satisfactory answer to this question first, before delving into any research of Islamic creed. For minds and intellects will not be prepared to receive the truths of tawḥīd (monotheism) and the creedal components of this religion unless the vision is cleared before them, and the path to them is purified of all impurities, obstacles, and impediments. So we say in answer to that: Indeed, Allah Almighty, when His will was attached to the creation of this universe including what it contains of types and kinds of existents, His dazzling wisdom required that He choose a type from these existents (which is man) and make him the master of this universe and make all its manifestations and existents subservient to him, serving him, and entrust to him its cultivation and the matter of its organization. That is the meaning of vicegerency (khilāfah) in His saying: "And [mention] when your Lord said to the angels, 'Indeed, I am going to place upon the earth a vicegerent'" [Al-Baqarah: 30]. And it is what is intended by 'settlement' (istiʿmār) in His saying: "He has produced you from the earth and settled you in it" [Hūd: 61]. Man is equipped with the most dangerous qualities and faculties: So He equipped this creature with a set of faculties and qualities, necessary for him, so that his ability to manage the affairs of this universe, cultivate it, and use it may be complete. So He instilled in him the quality of intellect (ʿaql) and what branches from it of knowledge, perception, ability to analyze things, probe their depths, and reach what lies beyond them. And He instilled in him the meaning of selfishness (anāniyyah) and what branches from it of inclination to egoism and possession. And He instilled in him the causes of strength and the components of management, and what branches from them of inclination to control, greatness, and status. Then He instilled in him a set of emotions, longings, and reactions that complement the value of those qualities and their benefits, such as love, hatred, anger, and so on. And you are aware that man was not able to subjugate anything in this universe or control anything of the affairs and manifestations of life except on the day that Allah Almighty equipped him with these faculties and qualities. However, these qualities have great harm and grave maladies. They are double-edged weapons: if one edge is used, it brings great organization to the universe and abundant good for man; but if the other edge is used, or both are used together, that brings malignant evil, immense chaos, and bequeaths to humanity endless misery.
Source pages p. 64

Commentary
This passage is an objection-and-answer unit. It begins by presenting a common objection against the need for religion, then provides a detailed answer based on divine wisdom. The objection is posed by those lacking Islamic culture: Why would God burden us with religion rather than leave us free? The objector extends this to question why God needs our worship. The author notes a methodological principle: such questions cannot be answered if the questioner denies God's existence; rather, the proper approach is to first establish God's existence. However, for the benefit of a believing researcher, the author proceeds. The answer begins by stating God's wisdom in creating the universe: He chose man as vicegerent (khalīfah) and subjugated all other things to him, entrusting him with its cultivation and organization. This is supported by Quranic verses (Al-Baqarah 2:30 and Hūd 11:61). Then the author explains that to fulfill this role, man was equipped with specific faculties: intellect (ʿaql) and its branches (knowledge, perception, analysis), selfishness (anāniyyah) leading to egoism, strength and management leading to desire for control, and emotions (love, hate, anger). These faculties are necessary for man to subjugate the universe. However, they are double-edged: if used properly, they bring order and good; if used improperly, they bring chaos and misery. This implicitly shows the need for divine guidance (religion) to ensure correct use of these faculties.

أنانية
ملكات
صفات

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that the question about the need for religion can be answered directly without first establishing God's existence.
Correction: Buti emphasizes the methodological priority of proving God's existence before addressing such objections, as the objection itself often presupposes atheism.

Checkpoint
According to Buti, why did God equip man with intellect, selfishness, strength, and emotions?
A) To test man's obedience through these faculties
B) To enable man to fulfill his role as vicegerent by managing and cultivating the universe
C) To make man superior to angels
D) To allow man to live independently of divine guidance

Key Takeaway
Religion is necessary not because God needs our worship, but because our God-given faculties for managing the world are double-edged and require divine guidance to produce order and good.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Which of your God-given faculties (intellect, ambition, strength, emotions) have you most often used in a way that brings chaos rather than order? When has selfishness or anger led you to harm someone or neglect your responsibilities as God's vicegerent?
?
If you truly believed that your intellect and desires are 'double-edged weapons' that require divine guidance to use correctly, what would change about how you approach your daily decisions—especially in moments of anger or greed? Are you, right now, actively seeking that guidance or ignoring it?
?
God placed you on this earth as His deputy to cultivate and organize it. In what area of your life (work, family, community) are you contributing to disorder or destruction instead of building? What is one concrete step you will take today to realign your use of your faculties with the purpose for which God gave them to you?

The Three Components of Islamic Structure and the Primacy of Creed
Defines and ranks the three elements of Islamic structure.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the three components of the Islamic structure and why creed is considered the indispensable foundation.

Core Idea
Creed is the foundation of Islam; without it, deeds are worthless.

This passage from a contemporary scholar breaks down the Islamic structure into three elements: creed, legislation, and morals. The author argues that while all three are important, creed holds primary status. Even if one's deeds are lacking, sound creed makes one a Muslim, but the reverse is not true. Let's read the original text to grasp this key principle.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three components
Read the opening sentence and list the three elements that constitute the Islamic structure according to the author.
They are عقيدة, تشريع, and أخلاق.
2
Understand the primacy of creed
Notice how the author argues that creed is the foundation. Pay attention to the two conditional scenarios: having creed with deficient deeds vs. having deeds without creed.
The author uses strong language: 'if the creed fills the heart, its possessor is thereby a Muslim'.
3
Reflect on the Quranic evidence
Read the quoted verses (Al-Kahf 103-105) and see how they support the argument that deeds without correct creed are futile.
The verse describes those whose efforts are wasted despite appearing to do good.

من أجل ذلك ، صح أن يطلق الدين على العقيدة وحدها ، إذ هي أساس الأمر كله ، فيقال : فلان يدين بالإسلام أو اعتنق الإسلام ، إذا رأيته قد صدق واعترف بعقيدته كاملة من غير تبديل أو نقص ، واستسلم يقينه لجميع أركانه ولا يشترط لصحة هذه التسمية أن يكون ذلك مصحوباً بسلوك عملي في شؤون العبادة أو سائر الأحكام الشرعية الأخرى وإن كان التقصير في شيء منها موجبـاً للفسق ومعرضاً بناء العقيدة نفسها للزلازل
The Islamic structure consists of three elements: creed, legislation, and morals. The Islamic meaning is completed for the Muslim by sound creed when it settles in his heart, by following his legislation in all his dealings with God and with people, and then by virtuous morals upon which he builds his relationship with others. However, the support of all that is creed, for it is the first foundation that is indispensable. So much so that if this creed fills the heart, its possessor is thereby a Muslim, even if he falls short in applying the other two elements. But he thereby incurs sin that exposes him to God's punishment. But if the creed is not complete in his certainty and perception, then he is not considered a Muslim, even if he spends his entire life in worship and acts of obedience and colors all his conduct with the rulings and etiquette of sharia. And concerning such people was the revelation of God's words: 'Say: Shall We inform you who are the greatest losers in their works? Those whose effort is lost in the worldly life while they think that they are doing good. Those are who disbelieve in the signs of their Lord and in the meeting with Him, so their works become worthless, and We will not assign to them on the Day of Resurrection any weight.' (Al-Kahf: 103-105) Therefore, it is correct to apply the word 'religion' to creed alone, for it is the basis of the whole matter. So it is said: 'So-and-so adheres to Islam' or 'embraced Islam' if you see that he has affirmed and acknowledged his creed completely without alteration or deficiency, and his certainty has surrendered to all its pillars. And the validity of this designation does not require that it be accompanied by practical behavior in matters of worship or other legal rulings, even if deficiency in any of them causes sin and exposes the very edifice of creed to tremors.
Source pages p. 70

Commentary
This passage defines the three components of the Islamic structure and argues for the primacy of creed. It begins by listing the three elements: creed (العقيدة), legislation (التشريع), and morals (الأخلاق). The author then explains that the Islamic meaning is completed through sound creed settling in the heart, following the sharia in dealings, and virtuous morals in relationships. However, the main point is that creed is the foundation: if a person has correct creed in his heart, he is considered a Muslim even if he falls short in the other two elements, though he incurs sin. Conversely, if creed is missing, he is not a Muslim even if he performs all acts of worship and follows the sharia outwardly. The author supports this with the Quranic verse about those whose efforts are wasted despite seeming to do good (Al-Kahf 103-105). Therefore, the term 'religion' can be applied to creed alone, and one is called a Muslim if he acknowledges and affirms the creed fully, regardless of practical compliance, though deficiency in practice is sinful and can weaken the creed's structure.

أخلاق

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Performing religious duties and good deeds alone is sufficient to be considered a Muslim, even without correct creed.
Correction: The passage explicitly states that without complete creed in certainty, one is not a Muslim regardless of deeds.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the criterion for being considered a Muslim?
A) Performing all acts of worship and following sharia
B) Possessing sound creed in the heart, even if deficient in deeds
C) Possessing good morals and ethics
D) Combining creed, legislation, and morals equally

Key Takeaway
True Islam is fundamentally about correct creed; deeds perfect it but do not replace it.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?

?
Are there any beliefs in your heart that contradict the core creed? How will you seek to purify them, starting today?

Method of Learning
beginner
3 min
Every Truth Depends on a Self-Evident Truth
States the foundational principle of avoiding infinite regress.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why every chain of reasoning must ultimately rest on self-evident truths to avoid infinite regress.

Core Idea
All knowledge chains anchor in self-evident truths.

Sanusi establishes a crucial epistemological principle: no proof can go on forever. Every argument, no matter how sophisticated, depends on foundational truths that are immediately known and require no further proof. This principle is the bedrock of the top-down method of reasoning about Allah and creation.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once, then the translation. Notice the conditional structure: 'otherwise the researcher would remain seeking the proof.'
This is a single, dense sentence containing a complete argument.
2
Understand the problem of infinite regress
The passage implies that if every truth required proof, then each proof would itself need proof, leading to an endless chain. This is the problem of infinite regress.
3
Grasp the solution: self-evident truths
The solution is to have truths that are self-evident, requiring no proof. They serve as the foundation for all other truths.
These self-evident truths are often called 'necessary truths' or 'بديهيات'.
4
Reflect on why this matters for theology
In Islamic theology (kalam), this principle justifies starting with necessary truths about existence, causality, and the impossibility of an infinite chain of causes.
This method is called the 'top-down' approach, beginning with self-evident premises.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كل حقيقة علمية مهما دقت ، لابد أن تعتمد في نهاية الأمر ، على حقيقة ضرورية ) أي بدهية ( لا تحتاج إلى برهان ، وإلا لظل الباحث يطلب البرهان
Every scientific truth, no matter how subtle, must in the final analysis depend on a necessary truth (i.e., self-evident) that does not need a proof, otherwise the researcher would remain seeking the proof.
Source pages p. 78

Commentary
This passage states a key epistemological principle that underlies the top-down method: every truth ultimately rests on self-evident (necessary) truths that require no proof. If this were not the case, an infinite regress of proofs would occur. This principle justifies starting with direct reflection on necessary truths about existence and causality.

Key Terms
حقيقة علمية
حقيقة ضرورية
بدهية
برهان

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: This means that all truths are self-evident.
Correction: No, the passage only states that the chain of reasoning must end in self-evident truths. Most truths are not self-evident but are derived from them.

Checkpoint
According to this passage, why must every truth ultimately depend on a self-evident truth?
A) Because otherwise the researcher would become confused.
B) Because without it, the researcher would keep demanding proofs endlessly.
C) Because the Quran commands it.
D) Because it is a principle of modern science.

Key Takeaway
Rational knowledge rests on foundational self-evident truths to prevent infinite regress.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Think of one belief you hold about your purpose in life. Ask yourself: does that belief ultimately rest on a self-evident truth, or is it built on assumptions you have never examined? If you traced it back to its foundation, would you find solid ground—or a chain that never ends? Call yourself to account: Are you willing to follow that chain wherever it leads, even if it challenges how you live today?
?
When you face a doubt about your faith, your inclination might be to look for yet another proof. But this lesson says that at some point, you must accept a starting point. What is that non-negotiable, self-evident truth for you? Write it down. Then ask yourself: Does your life actually rest on that truth, or have you been trying to prove everything else while ignoring the ground beneath your feet?

The Two Methods of Gradual Reasoning
Buti describes two methodological approaches: tadarruj min al-a'la and tadarruj min al-adna.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand two complementary methodological approaches to establishing certainty in matters of faith: the path of gradual descent from the highest and the path of gradual ascent from the lowest.

Core Idea
Certainty can be reached from above or below—both lead to the same Truth.

In this passage, Ramadan al-Buti presents two distinct yet complementary ways of reasoning towards certainty in the fundamentals of faith. The first begins with established truths and descends to derive further beliefs, while the second starts with observable evidence and ascends to the ultimate source. Understanding both methods equips the student with a versatile toolkit for theological investigation.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without stopping. Notice the flow: first the description of one path, then the second. Let the author's own terms register.
Pay attention to the phrases 'طريق التدرج من الأعلى' and 'طريق التدرج من الأدنى'.
2
Identify the two methods
Locate where the first path is named and where the second path is named. Note what they start from and what they conclude.
The first starts from belief in messengers; the second starts from the Quran as a historical text.
3
Contrast the directions
Reflect on why one is called 'from the highest' and the other 'from the lowest'. How do they complement each other?
They are not opposed but offer different starting points for the same truth.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بدوره على صدق الرسل والأنبياء فيما بعثوا به من التكاليف ، ودلنا الإيمان بالرسل على الإيمان بالكتب وبالقرآن أنه كلام الله عز وجل ، ثم دلنـا الإيمان بكلام الله على الإيمان بكل ما تضمنه من أخبار وأحكام وأوامر ونواه ولنسم هذا الطريق بطريق التدرج من الأعلى

مختلفة

الطريق الثاني : ترك البحث في ذات الله ، والبدء بالنظر في خبر نقل إلينا عن حقيقة هذا الكتاب الذي بين يدينا والذي اسمه القرآن . حتى إذا علمنا بالبرهان اليقيني المتعلق بتحقيق النقول والأخبار أنه قد وصل إلينا بواسطة محمد ، وأنه قال عنه إنه وحي من الله عز وجل ، أخذنا نحقق في معنى الوحي كما فسره الرسول ولولا الله نفسه بالبراهين العلمية المنسجمة مع علوم هذه الدعوى ، وهي برهان التلازم البين وقياس الأولى طبق ما ذكرناه وبشروطه السالفة الاستقراء التام

وغيره
من
حتى إذا ثبت لدينا صدق دعوى الرسول مع الله وأن الوحي حقيقة لا اختيار وساء للرسول فيها وليس معنى شعورياً نابعاً من كيانه ، بحثنا فيما عسى أن يكون مصدراً لهذا الوحي ، ببرهان التلازم القائم على الاستقراء التام . حتى إذا ثبت لدينا بواسطة الاستقصاء أنه لا يمكن أن يكون لهذا الوحي مُنْزِل إلا الله جل جلاله ، دلنا ذلك على وجود الله عز وجل ، وازداد بذلك إيماننا بكل المراحل التي كنا قد اجتزناها بالبحث . ولنسم هذه الطريقة بطريق التدرج من الأدنى ولنبدأ الآن بالسير في الطريق الأول
In turn, [this leads to] belief in the messengers and prophets regarding what they were sent with of obligations, and belief in the messengers guided us to belief in the scriptures and in the Quran that it is the speech of Allah Almighty. Then belief in the speech of Allah guided us to belief in everything it contains of reports, rulings, commands, and prohibitions. And let us name this path the path of gradual descent from the highest. [different] The second path: abandoning investigation into the essence of Allah, and beginning with consideration of a report transmitted to us about the reality of this book which is in our hands and whose name is the Quran. Until we know by certain proof related to verification of the transmissions and reports that it has reached us by means of Muhammad, and that he said about it that it is revelation from Allah Almighty, we then investigate the meaning of revelation as the Messenger interpreted it—and Allah Himself—by scientific proofs consistent with the sciences of this claim, namely the proof of clear concomitance and the argument of priority according to what we mentioned and its earlier conditions of complete induction. and other from until the truthfulness of the messenger's claim with Allah is established for us, and that revelation is a reality, not a choice and not a subjective meaning emanating from his being, we investigate what could be the source of this revelation, by the proof of concomitance based on complete induction. Until it is established for us by exhaustive examination that there can be no sender of this revelation except Allah Almighty, that guides us to the existence of Allah Almighty, and thereby our faith increases in all the stages we had traversed through research. And let us name this method the path of gradual ascent from the lowest, and let us now begin to follow the first path.
Source pages p. 78

Commentary
This passage classifies two methodological approaches for achieving certainty in matters of faith. The author begins by describing the first path (tadarruj min al-a'la): starting from belief in the messengers, then in the scriptures, then in the Quran as God's speech, and then in all its contents. This is a deductive descent from higher principles. The second path (tadarruj min al-adna) starts from the empirical fact of the Quran as a historical text, then verifies its transmission through Muhammad, then investigates the nature of revelation, and finally arrives at the existence of God through the proof of concomitance. The author names both paths and announces his intention to begin with the first path. The intervening words 'مختلفة' and 'وغيره من' are likely OCR artifacts but do not disrupt the overall argument.

Key Terms
طريق التدرج من الأعلى
طريق التدرج من الأدنى
برهان التلازم
الاستقراء التام

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The two methods are contradictory and one must choose either the top-down or bottom-up approach.
Correction: The two methods are complementary; both are valid paths to the same certitude. Buti presents them as alternative starting points, not rivals.

Checkpoint
What are the two methodological approaches described in this passage?
A) Tadarruj min al-a'la (gradual descent from the highest) and tadarruj min al-adna (gradual ascent from the lowest)
B) Qiyas al-awla (argument of priority) and burhan al-talazum (proof of concomitance)
C) Istiqra' tamm (complete induction) and istiqsa' (exhaustive examination)
D) Al-iman bil-rusul (faith in messengers) and al-iman bil-kutub (faith in scriptures)

Key Takeaway
The two gradual methods—descending from the highest and ascending from the lowest—offer complementary routes to certainty about Allah and revelation.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Which of these two methods do you personally find more convincing, and why? Is your current faith built more on top-down certainty or bottom-up investigation?
?
The second method begins with doubt and rigorous verification. Are you willing to subject your own beliefs to that depth of scrutiny, even if it means temporarily unsettling what you hold certain?
?
Both methods lead to the same Truth, yet people often insist only one approach is valid. How does that insight challenge your attitude toward fellow believers who came to faith through a different path?

The Four Foundational Principles
Buti enumerates four innate principles and states they are self-evident proofs.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the four innate principles that serve as self-evident proofs for the existence of God.

Core Idea
Four self-evident truths provide the foundation for proving God's existence.

Buti begins by presenting the intellectual foundations upon which the direct proof of God's existence rests. These are not learned axioms but innate truths that rational minds recognize immediately. In this lesson, we will examine the four principles as enumerated by Buti and understand why scholars consider them necessary and self-proving.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analysis. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
2
Identify the four principles
The passage lists four principles. Write them down and reflect on their meaning.
3
Understand their status
Note that the author says these principles are themselves proofs (براهين نفسها) and that scholars agree on their necessity.
4
Connect to the bigger argument
These principles will be used to build the direct proof of God's existence through indication of correlation (دلالة التلازم).

Source Text

نضع أمامك ، في الجواب على ذلك ، جملة من الحقائق والمبادئ الفطرية التي أجمع العلماء على ضرورتها وعلى أنها هي ذاتها براهين نفسها ، ونقيم عليها البرهان المباشر على وجوده سبحانه وتعالى عن طريق دلالة التلازم البين الذي مر بك في منهج البحث ، هذه الحقائق هي

We place before you, in answer to that, a set of innate truths and principles whose necessity all scholars have agreed upon and that they are themselves proofs, and we establish upon them the direct proof of His existence, Most High, through the indication of the clear correlation that passed with you in the methodology of research. These truths are: 1. The impossibility of preponderance without a preponderator. 2. The impossibility of infinite regress. 3. The impossibility of circularity. (1) 4. The law of causality. (1) (1) You might object that many people – even their educated ones – have not heard of these terms and names, so how can it be true that they contain innate truths known to all rational people? The answer is that what is new and strange to them is only the expressions and terminologies. As for their contents, they are established and imprinted in the minds of all people, as you will find.
Source pages p. 79

Commentary
This passage introduces the four foundational principles that the author will use as proofs for God's existence. The author preemptively addresses an objection that many people (including intellectuals) are unfamiliar with these technical terms. The reply distinguishes between the formal expressions (which may be new) and their innate meanings (which are universally recognized). The passage emphasizes that these principles are self-evident (badihiyyah) and do not themselves require proof; they form the basis for demonstrative arguments.

Key Terms

Correction: Buti explicitly states that these principles are themselves proofs (براهين نفسها) and are recognized as necessary by all scholars, so they are foundational self-evident truths.

Checkpoint
What does Buti say about the status of these four principles?
A) They require external proof.
B) They are themselves proofs.
C) They are based on revelation.
D) They are learned from experience.

Key Takeaway
The four principles (impossibility of preponderance without preponderator, impossibility of infinite regress, impossibility of circularity, and causality) are self-evident truths that form the foundation for proving God's existence.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You rely on causality every time you light a match expecting fire. But when it comes to your own existence, do you accept that it too demands a cause? What would it mean for your life if you truly lived as though you were caused by a Creator? Are you ready to follow that logic to its end?
?
The principle of impossibility of infinite regress tells you that your lineage of causes stops at a First Cause. Yet you often act as if your actions have no ultimate consequence. How would your daily choices change if you remembered that your every deed is tied to that First Cause? Will you let this truth pierce your indifference?
?
These innate principles are etched into your mind by God, yet you might neglect them when they demand submission. Ask yourself: What is the real reason you avoid applying these truths to your own soul? Is it fear, pride, or comfort? Will you today allow these self-evident truths to humble you before your Creator?

The Objection on Terminology
Buti addresses an objection about the novelty of technical terms for innate truths.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the distinction between technical terms and innate meanings, and why unfamiliarity with terminology does not negate universal rational knowledge.

Core Idea
Technical terms may be new, but their meanings are innate in all minds.

Having listed the four foundational principles, Buti anticipates an objection: if these principles are truly innate, why are many people—even educated ones—unaware of their technical names? In this lesson, we explore Buti's response, which clarifies the difference between linguistic labels and the universal concepts they represent.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection
First, identify the objection raised: that many people have not heard of these terms, so how can they be innate?
2
Read Buti's answer
Buti distinguishes between the expressions (تعابير) and the contents (مضمونات). The terms may be new, but the meanings are imprinted in all minds.
3
Reflect on the implication
Consider how this defense protects the argument from the charge of being merely academic or esoteric.

(١) قد تستشكل بأن كثيراً من الناس - حتى مثقفيهم - لم يسمعوا بهذه الاصطلاحات والأسماء ، فكيف يصدق أنها تتضمن حقائق فطرية يعرفها العقلاء جميعاً ؟ والجواب أن الجديد والغريب عليهم إنما هو التعابير والاصطلاحات. أما مضموناتها مثبتة ومطبوعة في أذهان الناس جميعاً ، كما ستجد
We place before you, in answer to that, a set of innate truths and principles whose necessity all scholars have agreed upon and that they are themselves proofs, and we establish upon them the direct proof of His existence, Most High, through the indication of the clear correlation that passed with you in the methodology of research. These truths are: 1. The impossibility of preponderance without a preponderator. 2. The impossibility of infinite regress. 3. The impossibility of circularity. (1) 4. The law of causality. (1) (1) You might object that many people – even their educated ones – have not heard of these terms and names, so how can it be true that they contain innate truths known to all rational people? The answer is that what is new and strange to them is only the expressions and terminologies. As for their contents, they are established and imprinted in the minds of all people, as you will find.
Source pages p. 79

Commentary
This passage introduces the four foundational principles that the author will use as proofs for God's existence. The author preemptively addresses an objection that many people (including intellectuals) are unfamiliar with these technical terms. The reply distinguishes between the formal expressions (which may be new) and their innate meanings (which are universally recognized). The passage emphasizes that these principles are self-evident (badihiyyah) and do not themselves require proof; they form the basis for demonstrative arguments.

Correction: Buti clarifies that the concepts are innate and known to all, even if the specific terms are unfamiliar.

The Argument of Correlation and the Transition to Causality
Author declares God's existence proven by correlation argument and transitions to causality.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the argument of correlation (burhān al-talāzum) grounds the proof of God's existence through complete induction, and how the author transitions to the law of causality and syllogism as the next method of proof.

Core Idea
The argument of correlation, built on complete induction, establishes God's existence; causality is the next logical step.

This brief but pivotal passage summarises the conclusive proof of God's existence offered earlier and signals a shift in methodology. Before moving to the next argument, the author reaffirms that the argument of correlation, based on complete induction, has already provided certainty. He then introduces the law of causality (or final cause) and the syllogism as the next tool in the theological arsenal.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two main parts
The passage has a declarative conclusion and a transition. First, the author states that God's existence has appeared by a certain proof based on the argument of correlation and complete induction. Second, he introduces the law of causality and his intention to move from correlation to syllogism.
Notice the Arabic phrase 'قانون العلية أو العلة الغائية' – the author equates causality with final cause.
2
Understand the argument of correlation
The argument of correlation (burhān al-talāzum) is a logical proof that establishes a necessary connection between two things. Here it is grounded on complete induction (al-istiqrāʾ al-tāmm), meaning every observed instance confirms the correlation.
Complete induction is a strong inductive method that yields certainty.
3
Note the transition to causality
The author signals a shift from the correlation argument to a new form of reasoning: the law of causality and syllogism. This prepares the reader for a different type of proof based on final causes.
The phrase 'ولننتقل بعد هذا' means 'let us move after this'.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقد ظهر وجود الله عز وجل ، بالدليل اليقيني القائم على برهان التلازم المرتكز على الاستقراء التام .

قانون العلية أو « العلة الغائية » :
ولننتقل بعد هذا من برهان التلازم إلى القياس
And the existence of Allah, mighty and majestic, has appeared by the certain proof (al-dalīl al-yaqīnī) based on the argument of correlation (burhān al-talāzum) grounded on complete induction (al-istiqrāʾ al-tāmm).

The law of causality (qānūn al-ʿilliyya) or 'the final cause' (al-ʿilla al-ghāʾiyya):
And let us move after this from the argument of correlation to the syllogism (al-qiyās).
Source pages p. 88

Commentary
This passage serves as a transition. The author first declares that God's existence has been proven by a certain proof (dalīl yaqīnī) based on the argument of correlation (burhān al-talāzum), which itself rests on complete induction (istiqrāʾ tāmm). Then he introduces the next topic: the law of causality or final cause (al-ʿilla al-ghāʾiyya). He announces a shift from the argument of correlation to the syllogism (al-qiyās), indicating that a new argumentative method will be employed. The passage is methodological, summarising an accomplished proof and previewing the next stage of reasoning.

Key Terms

قانون العلية

قياس

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) Complete induction (al-istiqrāʾ al-tāmm).
C) The law of causality.
D) The syllogism.

Key Takeaway
The argument of correlation, grounded on complete induction, proves God's existence with certainty, and the author now turns to causality and syllogism as the next method.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

The author moves from correlation to causality. In your own life, do you see the order and purpose (final cause) in creation? Take a moment to reflect on one aspect of nature and ask yourself: Can I truly deny that there is a purposeful Creator behind it? Write down one observation that strengthens your certainty.
?
The argument here is based on complete induction—considering all cases. When it comes to your own life, are you consistent in applying Islamic principles to all situations, or do you pick and choose? This lesson calls for a comprehensive worldview. What is one area where you need to align your actions with the complete truth?

Introduction to the First Proof: The Clearest Cosmic Reality
Buti introduces the first method of proving God's existence as a clear cosmic reality.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Buti introduces the first proof of God's existence as a clear cosmic reality and why he deems it necessary to present proofs despite its clarity.

Core Idea
The existence of God is the clearest truth, but biased minds need proofs.

In this passage, Buti sets the stage for the first proof of God's existence. He emphasizes that the reality of God is the clearest and most momentous cosmic truth, but acknowledges that some minds are clouded by bias and require structured reasoning. This lesson explores the rationale behind offering proofs for such an evident reality.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Notice the tone: Buti states the reality is clear, yet he still presents a proof.
Pay attention to the contrast between 'fair intellect' and 'shackled minds'.
2
Identify the key claim
Find where Buti says the existence of God is the 'clearest and most momentous cosmic reality'. Think about what makes it 'clear' and 'momentous'.
3
Understand the need for proofs
Buti says fair minds do not need elaborate proofs, but biased minds do. Ask yourself: Why would bias prevent someone from seeing the clear truth? How does that justify presenting proofs?
The footnote references another book for a detailed refutation of materialism.

Source Text

الطريقة الأولى في الاستدلال على أوضح حقيقة كونية وأخطرها ، هذه ألا حقيقة وجود الله عز وجل . عرضناها عرضاً إجمالياً ينسجم مع طبيعة هذا الكتاب ؛ وطبيعة القارئ . وإن العقل المنصف الحر لفي غنى عن ترتيب كل تلك المقدمات والبراهين والموازين لولا أن ثمة عقولاً مكبلة بأغلال من الأغراض والاتجاهات تقتضيها أن تغمض العين وتصرف النظر .. فهي تظل تصطنع الشبه (١) إذا أردت أن تقف على خرافة الفكر المادي بتفصيل ، فارجع إلى كتاب نقض أوهام المادية الجدلية لمؤلف هذا الكتاب.
The first method of inferring the clearest and most momentous cosmic reality, which is the reality of the existence of God Almighty. We have presented it in a summary manner that harmonizes with the nature of this book and the nature of the reader. The fair and free intellect is in no need of arranging all those premises, proofs, and balances, were it not for the presence of minds shackled with chains of purposes and inclinations that require them to close their eyes and avert their gaze... so they continue to fabricate doubts. (1) If you wish to know the myth of materialist thought in detail, refer to the book 'Naqd Awham al-Madiyya al-Jadaliyya' by the author of this book.

Commentary
This passage introduces a new section: the first proof of God's existence. Buti states that the existence of God is the clearest and most important cosmic reality, and he presents it briefly for the book's scope. He acknowledges that fair-minded people would not need elaborate proofs, but he provides them because some minds are biased and deliberately ignore the truth, fabricating doubts. The footnote directs readers to his other book for a detailed refutation of materialist thought. This sets the stage for the proof that follows.

The First Method and Fabricated Doubts
Buti presents the first proof for God and addresses those who fabricate doubts.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Buti argues that rational proofs for God's existence are necessary despite it being self-evident, and how to address those who fabricate doubts.

Core Idea
Self-evident truths become contested only when minds are shackled by bias.

Buti begins by dismissing the search for material roots of thought as futile. He then introduces the first method of proving God's existence, noting that a free mind would not need it. However, because some minds are shackled by biases and deliberately fabricate doubts, we must engage with their objections. This passage sets the stage for why theological reasoning is needed.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the translation. Notice the contrast between the free mind and the shackled mind.
Pay attention to the emotional tone—Buti is both dismissive and serious.
2
Identify the two mindsets
Buti describes two types of people: those with free, impartial minds, and those shackled by interests and tendencies. Identify how each relates to the proof for God's existence.
The free mind doesn't need proofs; the shackled mind fabricates doubts.
3
Understand Buti's response strategy
Buti says we must take the matter seriously, treat self-evident truths as theoretical problems, and address the fabricators on their own terms. Reflect on why this approach is necessary.
He compares it to driving a liar beyond the door—a rhetorical dismissal.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وعبث لا طائل فيه أن تبحث للفكر عن جذور أو عوامل في دنيا المادة أو الاقتصاد أو وسيلة الإنتاج الطريقة الأولى في الاستدلال على أوضح حقيقة كونية وأخطرها ، هذه ألا حقيقة وجود الله عز وجل . عرضناها عرضاً إجمالياً ينسجم مع طبيعة هذا الكتاب ؛ وطبيعة القارئ . وإن العقل المنصف الحر لفي غنى عن ترتيب كل تلك المقدمات والبراهين والموازين لولا أن ثمة عقولاً مكبلة بأغلال من الأغراض والاتجاهات تقتضيها أن تغمض العين وتصرف النظر .. فهي تظل تصطنع الشبه اصطناعاً وتخترع المشكلات اختراعاً ، وتركب رأسها في مخاصمة البديهيات ومناقشة الضروريات . وبذلك تظهر مسألة وجود الله بين كثير من الفئات بمظهر الموضوع العلمي العويص الذي يكتنفه شبه ومشكلات كثيرة فهذه الظاهرة التى تلبست بعض العقول هي ! تدعو - كما قلنا في المقدمة - إلى أن نحمل الأمر على محمل الجد، وأن نقيل تمثيل الممثلين واصطناع المصطنعين ، ونفرض الأمر البدهي نظرياً والقضايا الفطرية معضلات فكرية فنخاطبهم بالطريقة ذاتها ، ونلحق الكذاب كما يقولون إلى ما وراء الباب ! ..
It is a futile and pointless exercise to search for roots or factors of thought in the world of matter, economics, or the means of production. The first method of reasoning for the clearest and most serious cosmic truth, namely the truth of the existence of God Almighty. We presented it in a general manner consistent with the nature of this book and the reader. And the impartial, free mind is in no need of arranging all those premises, proofs, and scales, were it not that there are minds shackled by the fetters of interests and tendencies that require them to close their eyes and turn away... They continue to fabricate doubts deliberately and invent problems artificially, and stubbornly engage in disputing self-evident truths and challenging necessary matters. Thus the issue of the existence of God appears to many groups in the guise of an abstruse scientific subject surrounded by many doubts and problems. This phenomenon that has infected some minds calls – as we said in the introduction – for us to take the matter seriously, to excuse the actors and the fabricators, and to present the self-evident truth theoretically and the innate propositions as intellectual dilemmas, and address them with the same method, and, as they say, drive the liar beyond the door!...
Source pages p. 103

Commentary
This passage first dismisses the search for material roots of thought as futile. Then it introduces the first method of proving God's existence but notes that it is only needed because some minds are shackled by bias and fabricate doubts. The author describes how these people deliberately oppose self-evident truths and create problems. The solution is to take their objections seriously, treat self-evident truths as theoretical problems, and address them on their own terms, ultimately dismissing the fabricators.

The Second Method of Proof: Gradual Ascent from the Quran
Buti introduces the second method, starting with the Quran as a transmitted book.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Buti's second method of proving God's existence, which begins with the Quran as a certain transmitted report and gradually ascends to the truth of God's existence.

Core Idea
The Quran itself is the starting point for a rational ascent to God.

In the previous lesson, Buti presented a direct method of proof. Now he introduces a complementary second method that starts from a tangible, historical reality: the Quran. This method does not abandon rationality but uses the Quran's certain transmission as a scientific fact, then progressively uncovers deeper truths. Let's read how he describes this gradual ascent.

Guided Path
1
Understand the need for a second method
Buti explains that he will not limit himself to the first method but will present a second one. This shows that multiple approaches are valid and complementary.
The second method is not independent but works alongside the first.
2
Grasp the process of gradual ascent
Read how the method starts from a manifest scientific issue, then through analysis reveals further issues, gradually leading to the ultimate truth of God's existence.
Think of this as a chain of reasoning where each step uncovers the next.
3
Apply the method to the Quran
Buti identifies the Quran as the initial manifest issue—a report-based matter. According to scientific method, we investigate its transmission.
This is a key shift: using transmitted knowledge as a starting point for rational proof.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
من أجل هذا لن نقتصر على عرض هذه الطريقة فيما انتهينا إليه ، بل نتجاوزها إلى الطريقة الثانية أيضاً ، وهي الطريقة التي تبدأ بمرحلة الخبر اليقيني ، وهي التي سميناها : طريق التدرج من الادنى وكما قلت لك . فإن هذه الطريقة الثانية تبدأ بالنظر في مسألة علمية ماثلة أمامنا ، حتى إذا انتهينا من تفسيرها ، انكشف لنا من ورائها مسألة أخرى متعلقة بها ، فإذا نظرنا فيها هي ! أيضاً وانتهينا من تحليلها ، انكشفت لنا مسألة عن ثالثة، حتى تتدرج بنا هذه المسائل إلى إثبات الحقيقة ذاتها التي ظهر ثبوتها لنا آنفاً ، وهي حقيقة وجود الله عز وجل نحن الآن أمام كتاب غريب اسمه ( القرآن ( تناقلته إلينا أيدي القرون من مصدر معين ، إذاً فنحن أمام مسألة خبرية تجسدت في صورة هذا الكتاب وعلينا أن نبدأ في تحقيقها حسب المنهج العلمي المتبع للتحقيق في النقول والأخبار . ولدى التحقيق . نعلم بأن هذا الكتاب وصل إلينا ( بسند صحيح متواتر -1.2_
For this reason, we will not confine ourselves to presenting this method as we have done, but will go beyond it to the second method as well, which is the method that begins with the stage of certain report (al-khabar al-yaqini), and which we have called: the way of gradual ascent from the lower. Then if we look into it as well and finish analyzing it, a third issue is revealed to us, until these issues gradually lead us to the proof of the very truth whose certainty appeared to us earlier, namely the truth of the existence of God Almighty. We are now before a strange book called the Quran, which the hands of centuries have transmitted to us from a specific source. So we are before a report-based issue (mas'ala khabariyya) embodied in the form of this book. We must begin to investigate it according to the scientific method followed for investigating transmissions and reports. Upon investigation, we know that this book has reached us with a sound, mutawatir chain of transmission -1.2_

The author identifies the Quran as a report-based issue and states that it should be investigated using the scientific method for examining transmissions. Introduction to the Path of Gradual Ascent
Buti introduces the second method and its step-by-step progression.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the overall structure of the second method (tariq al-tadarruj) and its starting point as a chain of questions leading to God.

Core Idea
The second method climbs from a tangible fact to God through linked questions.

Buti now presents a second method that does not start abstractly but from a concrete, transmitted fact—the Qur'an. This method gradually ascends through a series of connected questions, each leading to the next, until the truth of God's existence is reached. The passage outlines the general approach before diving into specifics.

Guided Path
1
Understand the method's name and logic
The term 'gradual ascent from the lowest' means starting from something accessible and moving upward. Here 'lowest' refers to a well-known report (the Qur'an).
This is a methodological choice to begin with something that is widely accepted.
2
Notice the chain of questions
Buti describes a process: a scientific question leads to another related question, then another, until the final truth emerges. Try to visualize this as a staircase.
3
Identify the endpoint
The ultimate goal is proving the truth of God's existence, which the first method already established. This method provides a different route to the same conclusion.
Buti assumes the existence of God is already known from the first method; this is a complementary approach.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
من أجل هذا لن نقتصر على عرض هذه الطريقة فيما انتهينا إليه، بل نتجاوزها إلى الطريقة الثانية أيضاً، وهي الطريقة التي تبدأ بمرحلة الخبر اليقيني، والتي سميناها: طريق التدرج من الأدنى. وكما قلت لك، فإن هذه الطريقة الثانية تبدأ بالنظر في مسألة علمية ماثلة أمامنا، حتى إذا انتهينا من تفسيرها، انكشف لنا من ورائها مسألة أخرى متعلقة بها، فإذا نظرنا فيها هي أيضاً وانتهينا من تحليلها، انكشفت لنا مسألة عن ثالثة، حتى تتدرج بنا هذه المسائل إلى إثبات الحقيقة ذاتها التي ظهر ثبوتها لنا آنفاً، وهي حقيقة وجود الله عز وجل. نحن الآن أمام كتاب غريب اسمه (القرآن) تناقلته إلينا أيدي القرون من مصدر معين، إذاً فنحن أمام مسألة خبرية تجسدت في صورة هذا الكتاب، وعلينا أن نبدأ في تحقيقها حسب المنهج العلمي المتبع للتحقيق في النقول والأخبار. ولدى التحقيق، نعلم بأن هذا الكتاب وصل إلينا (بسند صحيح متواتر لا يخضع لإمكان الكذب في روايته) عن رجل اسمه محمد بن عبد الله صلى الله عليه وسلم ظهر في غضون القرن السادس الميلادي في الجزيرة العربية. كما نعلم لدى التحقيق في ذلك أيضاً بأن الرواية الصحيحة المتواترة أثبتت أنه كان يقول بأن هذا الكتاب ليس تأليفه وليس له كسب في شيء منه، وإنما هو يتلقاه وحياً من الله بواسطة من جبريل عليه السلام. فإذا انتهينا من تحقيق كل من هذين الخبرين، وجدنا أنفسنا أمام مسألة علمية أخرى هي ظاهرة هذا الوحي الذي أخبر عنه محمد صلى الله عليه وسلم فما هي حقيقته؟ وما الفرق بينه وبين الإلهام النفسي؟ وما مدى الاحتمالات العقلية للكذب في هذه الدعوى؟ فهذه قضية علمية أخرى ليست نقلاً حتى يكون تحقيقه عن طريق الرواية والسند، وليست حقيقة مادية محسوسة حتى يكون تحقيقها عن طريق التجربة المحسوسة المشاهدة، وإنما هي من قبيل القضايا العقلية المجردة، فليس من سبيل للتحقيق في أمرها إلا سبيل برهاني اللزوم البين والقياس اليقيني الأولى القائمين على الاستقراء التام. ونحن عندما نحقق في (ظاهرة الوحي) على هذا الأساس، نضطر إلى القطع بأن الوحي لم يكن شعوراً داخلياً ساور محمداً عليه الصلاة والسلام، وبأنه لم يكذب على الناس فيما قال، وبأن أحداً ممن كان في عصره لم يكن يختبئ خلفه ليعلمه هذا الذي يقول عنه إنه وحي من الله، وبأنه لا يمكن أن يكون وسوسة جن أو شياطين؛ نضطر إلى القطع بنفي هذه الاحتمالات بدليل التلازم والقياس الأولى والاستقراء الدقيق التام. وأنت تعلم أن المكان الملائم لتفصيل هذه البراهين وعرضها عند البحث في قسم النبوات الآتي قريباً إن شاء الله، وإنما نحن هنا نصور خطوات البحث ومراحله وكيفية التدرج من الأدنى إلى النهاية التي سنكتشفها. فإذا انتهينا من التحقيق في الوحي بهذا الشكل، وجدنا أنفسنا أمام ضرورة
For this reason we will not restrict ourselves to presenting this method in what we have concluded, but we will go beyond it to the second method as well, which is the method that begins with the stage of certain report (al-khabar al-yaqini), which we called: the path of gradual ascent from the lowest (tariq al-tadarruj min al-adna). And as I told you, this second method begins by looking into a present scientific question before us, until when we finish explaining it, another question related to it is revealed to us from behind it. Then if we look into it as well and finish analyzing it, a third question is revealed to us, until these questions gradually advance us to proving the very truth that has already appeared to us, which is the truth of the existence of God Almighty. We are now before a strange book called (the Qur'an) which the hands of centuries have transmitted to us from a specific source. So we are before a matter of report (mas'ala khabariyya) embodied in the form of this book, and we must begin to investigate it according to the scientific methodology followed for investigating transmitted reports and news. Upon investigation, we know that this book reached us (with a sound, mutawatir chain that is not subject to the possibility of lying in its transmission) from a man named Muhammad ibn Abdullah, may God bless him and grant him peace, who appeared during the sixth century CE in the Arabian Peninsula. We also know from investigation that the sound, mutawatir report also established that he used to say that this book is not his authorship and he has no acquisition in any part of it, but rather he receives it as revelation (wahy) from God through the agency of Gabriel, peace be upon him. When we finish investigating both of these reports, we find ourselves before another scientific question, which is the phenomenon of this revelation that Muhammad, may God bless him and grant him peace, informed about. So what is its reality? What is the difference between it and psychological inspiration (al-ilham al-nafsi)? What are the extent of the rational possibilities of lying in this claim? This is another scientific issue that is not a transmission so that its investigation be through narration and chain, nor is it a material sensed reality so that its investigation be through sensed observed experiment, but rather it is of the kind of abstract rational issues (al-qadaya al-'aqliyya al-mujarrada). So there is no way to investigate its matter except through the demonstrative way of clear implication (burhan al-luzum al-bayyin) and the primary certain syllogism (al-qiyas al-yaqini al-awwali) based on complete induction (al-istiqra' al-tamm). And when we investigate (the phenomenon of revelation) on this basis, we are compelled to conclude that the revelation was not an internal feeling that occurred to Muhammad, peace and blessings be upon him, and that he did not lie to people in what he said, and that no one from his era was hiding behind him to teach him this which he says is revelation from God, and that it cannot be the whispering of a jinn or devils. We are compelled to negate these possibilities by the proof of implication (dalil al-talazum), primary syllogism, and precise complete induction. And you know that the appropriate place for detailing these proofs and presenting them is in the upcoming section on prophethood, God willing. And here we are only depicting the steps of research and its stages and how to gradually ascend from the lowest to the end that we will discover. And when we finish investigating revelation in this way, we find ourselves before a necessity...
Source pages p. 104

Commentary
This passage introduces the second method of proving God's existence: the path of gradual ascent from the lowest (tariq al-tadarruj min al-adna). Buti explains that unlike the first method (not detailed here), this second method starts from a certain report (khabar yaqini)—specifically the Qur'an. It begins by examining a tangible 'scientific question' (here the Qur'an as a transmitted book) and then proceeds from one question to another, each related to the previous, until it reaches the ultimate truth of God's existence. The method is described as a chain: first, investigate the Qur'an as a historical report; second, investigate its claimed source (revelation); third, use rational proofs to determine the true nature of revelation; and finally, the conclusion that revelation is truly from God, thus establishing His existence. Buti emphasizes the methodological shift: the first question (the Qur'an) is a matter of transmission (khabar), investigated by chains of narration. Upon confirming that it comes with a sound, mutawatir chain from Muhammad (PBUH) who claimed it is revelation, we then face a second question: the reality of revelation itself. This is not a matter of transmission or empirical observation, but a rational issue. Therefore, it requires demonstrative proofs such as the proof of clear implication (burhan al-luzum al-bayyin), primary certain syllogism (al-qiyas al-yaqini al-awwali), and complete induction (al-istiqra' al-tamm). Using these, we can rule out all alternative explanations (internal feeling, lying, human teaching, demonic whispers) and conclude that revelation is true, leading to the necessity of God's existence. Buti notes that detailed proofs will be given in the later section on prophethood, so here he only outlines the steps.

Key Terms
طريق التدرج من الأدنى
الخبر اليقيني

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the starting point of the second method according to Buti?
A) Rational arguments for the necessity of a creator
B) The empirical observation of natural phenomena
C) The stage of certain report (al-khabar al-yaqini)
D) Direct intuition of the divine

Key Takeaway
The second method starts from a certain, transmitted fact and progresses through linked questions to prove God's existence.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever experienced a chain of questions in your own life that led you to a deeper certainty about God? What was that starting question?
?
Buti describes a method that begins with a 'certain report'—the Qur'an. Do you treat the Qur'an as such a certain starting point in your daily life, or do you often begin with your own doubts? What would change if you truly started from that certainty?
?
This method requires patience to move through linked questions. In your spiritual journey, are you willing to follow such a patient, step-by-step path, or do you expect immediate answers? What is holding you back from taking the first step?

Method of Learning
beginner
4 min
Investigating the Qur'an as a Certain Report
Buti investigates the Qur'an as a historical report and extracts two certain conclusions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the Qur'an is investigated as a historical report and what the investigation reveals about its transmission and claimed source.

Core Idea
The Qur'an reaches us through an unbroken chain that precludes lies.

After introducing the method, Buti now applies it to the first concrete question: the Qur'an itself. He treats it as a transmitted report that must be verified according to scientific methods of historical investigation. The passage shows how this verification leads to two key facts: the Qur'an's sound transmission from Muhammad (PBUH) and Muhammad's claim that it is divine revelation.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and identify the two findings
The passage presents two results of investigating the Qur'an: (1) it reached us via a sound mutawatir chain from Muhammad, and (2) Muhammad said it is revelation from God. Note how each is established.
The investigation uses the methodology of verifying transmissions (riwaya) and chains (sanad).
2
Understand the significance of 'mutawatir'
'Mutawatir' means reported by so many people at every level that it is impossible for them to have conspired to lie. This gives certainty.
3
Notice the shift from book to claim
Once we have the book as a fact, we move to the next question: the claim of revelation. This is a new issue that requires a different type of investigation.
This sets up the next lesson.

Method of Learning
intermediate
6 min
Revelation as a Rational Issue: Proofs and Certainty
Buti argues that revelation must be investigated rationally and uses proofs to rule out all alternative explanations.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the phenomenon of revelation is a rational issue and how demonstrative proofs (clear implication, primary syllogism, complete induction) eliminate all alternative explanations, compelling the conclusion that revelation is true.

Core Idea
Revelation is proven true by eliminating all other rational possibilities.

Having established that Muhammad claimed revelation, Buti now shifts from historical investigation to rational analysis. The phenomenon of revelation cannot be verified by chains of transmission or empirical observation; it requires abstract reasoning. Buti outlines the proofs that will be detailed later, showing how they rule out every possible alternative—internal feeling, lying, human tutoring, or demonic influence—leaving only the truth of divine revelation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the nature of the new question
Buti says revelation is not a transmission (naql) nor a material sensation, but a rational issue (qadiyya 'aqliyya). This determines the method of investigation.
2
List the alternative explanations
The passage enumerates four possibilities that must be negated: internal feeling, lying, a hidden human teacher, and jinn/devil whispering. Each is eliminated by rational proofs.
These are the only logical alternatives to genuine revelation.
3
Understand the proofs used
Buti mentions three types of proofs: burhan al-luzum al-bayyin (clear implication), al-qiyas al-yaqini al-awwali (primary certain syllogism), and al-istiqra' al-tamm (complete induction). These are demonstrated through analysis of Muhammad's life and the Qur'an.
Detailed proofs are promised in the later section on prophethood.
4
Note the conclusion
After eliminating alternatives, we are compelled to accept that revelation is true, which leads to the necessity of God's existence (though the passage cuts off).
This is the second step of the gradual ascent.

مسألة خبرية تجسدت في صورة هذا الكتاب، وعلينا أن نبدأ في تحقيقها حسب المنهج العلمي المتبع للتحقيق في النقول والأخبار. ولدى التحقيق، نعلم بأن هذا الكتاب وصل إلينا (بسند صحيح متواتر لا يخضع لإمكان الكذب في روايته) عن رجل اسمه محمد بن عبد الله صلى الله عليه وسلم ظهر في غضون القرن السادس الميلادي في الجزيرة العربية. كما نعلم لدى التحقيق في ذلك أيضاً بأن الرواية الصحيحة المتواترة أثبتت أنه كان يقول بأن هذا الكتاب ليس تأليفه وليس له كسب في شيء منه، وإنما هو يتلقاه وحياً من الله بواسطة من جبريل عليه السلام. فإذا انتهينا من تحقيق كل من هذين الخبرين، وجدنا أنفسنا أمام مسألة علمية أخرى هي ظاهرة هذا الوحي الذي أخبر عنه محمد صلى الله عليه وسلم فما هي حقيقته؟ وما الفرق بينه وبين الإلهام النفسي؟ وما مدى الاحتمالات العقلية للكذب في هذه الدعوى؟ فهذه قضية علمية أخرى ليست نقلاً حتى يكون تحقيقه عن طريق الرواية والسند، وليست حقيقة مادية محسوسة حتى يكون تحقيقها عن طريق التجربة المحسوسة المشاهدة، وإنما هي من قبيل القضايا العقلية المجردة، فليس من سبيل للتحقيق في أمرها إلا سبيل برهاني اللزوم البين والقياس اليقيني الأولى القائمين على الاستقراء التام. ونحن عندما نحقق في (ظاهرة الوحي) على هذا الأساس، نضطر إلى القطع بأن الوحي لم يكن شعوراً داخلياً ساور محمداً عليه الصلاة والسلام، وبأنه لم يكذب على الناس فيما قال، وبأن أحداً ممن كان في عصره لم يكن يختبئ خلفه ليعلمه هذا الذي يقول عنه إنه وحي من الله، وبأنه لا يمكن أن يكون وسوسة جن أو شياطين؛ نضطر إلى القطع بنفي هذه الاحتمالات بدليل التلازم والقياس الأولى والاستقراء الدقيق التام. وأنت تعلم أن المكان الملائم لتفصيل هذه البراهين وعرضها عند البحث في قسم النبوات الآتي قريباً إن شاء الله، وإنما نحن هنا نصور خطوات البحث ومراحله وكيفية التدرج من الأدنى إلى النهاية التي سنكتشفها. فإذا انتهينا من التحقيق في الوحي بهذا الشكل، وجدنا أنفسنا أمام ضرورة
For this reason we will not restrict ourselves to presenting this method in what we have concluded, but we will go beyond it to the second method as well, which is the method that begins with the stage of certain report (al-khabar al-yaqini), which we called: the path of gradual ascent from the lowest (tariq al-tadarruj min al-adna). And as I told you, this second method begins by looking into a present scientific question before us, until when we finish explaining it, another question related to it is revealed to us from behind it. Then if we look into it as well and finish analyzing it, a third question is revealed to us, until these questions gradually advance us to proving the very truth that has already appeared to us, which is the truth of the existence of God Almighty. We are now before a strange book called (the Qur'an) which the hands of centuries have transmitted to us from a specific source. So we are before a matter of report (mas'ala khabariyya) embodied in the form of this book, and we must begin to investigate it according to the scientific methodology followed for investigating transmitted reports and news. Upon investigation, we know that this book reached us (with a sound, mutawatir chain that is not subject to the possibility of lying in its transmission) from a man named Muhammad ibn Abdullah, may God bless him and grant him peace, who appeared during the sixth century CE in the Arabian Peninsula. We also know from investigation that the sound, mutawatir report also established that he used to say that this book is not his authorship and he has no acquisition in any part of it, but rather he receives it as revelation (wahy) from God through the agency of Gabriel, peace be upon him. When we finish investigating both of these reports, we find ourselves before another scientific question, which is the phenomenon of this revelation that Muhammad, may God bless him and grant him peace, informed about. So what is its reality? What is the difference between it and psychological inspiration (al-ilham al-nafsi)? What are the extent of the rational possibilities of lying in this claim? This is another scientific issue that is not a transmission so that its investigation be through narration and chain, nor is it a material sensed reality so that its investigation be through sensed observed experiment, but rather it is of the kind of abstract rational issues (al-qadaya al-'aqliyya al-mujarrada). So there is no way to investigate its matter except through the demonstrative way of clear implication (burhan al-luzum al-bayyin) and the primary certain syllogism (al-qiyas al-yaqini al-awwali) based on complete induction (al-istiqra' al-tamm). And when we investigate (the phenomenon of revelation) on this basis, we are compelled to conclude that the revelation was not an internal feeling that occurred to Muhammad, peace and blessings be upon him, and that he did not lie to people in what he said, and that no one from his era was hiding behind him to teach him this which he says is revelation from God, and that it cannot be the whispering of a jinn or devils. We are compelled to negate these possibilities by the proof of implication (dalil al-talazum), primary syllogism, and precise complete induction. And you know that the appropriate place for detailing these proofs and presenting them is in the upcoming section on prophethood, God willing. And here we are only depicting the steps of research and its stages and how to gradually ascend from the lowest to the end that we will discover. And when we finish investigating revelation in this way, we find ourselves before a necessity...
Source pages p. 104

Commentary
This passage introduces the second method of proving God's existence: the path of gradual ascent from the lowest (tariq al-tadarruj min al-adna). Buti explains that unlike the first method (not detailed here), this second method starts from a certain report (khabar yaqini)—specifically the Qur'an. It begins by examining a tangible 'scientific question' (here the Qur'an as a transmitted book) and then proceeds from one question to another, each related to the previous, until it reaches the ultimate truth of God's existence. The method is described as a chain: first, investigate the Qur'an as a historical report; second, investigate its claimed source (revelation); third, use rational proofs to determine the true nature of revelation; and finally, the conclusion that revelation is truly from God, thus establishing His existence. Buti emphasizes the methodological shift: the first question (the Qur'an) is a matter of transmission (khabar), investigated by chains of narration. Upon confirming that it comes with a sound, mutawatir chain from Muhammad (PBUH) who claimed it is revelation, we then face a second question: the reality of revelation itself. This is not a matter of transmission or empirical observation, but a rational issue. Therefore, it requires demonstrative proofs such as the proof of clear implication (burhan al-luzum al-bayyin), primary certain syllogism (al-qiyas al-yaqini al-awwali), and complete induction (al-istiqra' al-tamm). Using these, we can rule out all alternative explanations (internal feeling, lying, human teaching, demonic whispers) and conclude that revelation is true, leading to the necessity of God's existence. Buti notes that detailed proofs will be given in the later section on prophethood, so here he only outlines the steps.

Key Terms
برهان اللزوم البين
القياس اليقيني الأولى
الاستقراء التام
ظاهرة الوحي

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think revelation can be verified by empirical science or historical reports alone.
Correction: Buti clarifies that revelation is an abstract rational issue, requiring demonstrative proofs, not sensory or transmitted evidence.

Checkpoint
According to Buti, what kind of proofs are needed to investigate the phenomenon of revelation?
A) Proofs based on chains of transmission
B) Proofs based on empirical observation
C) Proofs of clear implication, primary syllogism, and complete induction
D) Proofs based on personal intuition

Key Takeaway
The truth of revelation is established by rationally eliminating all alternative explanations using demonstrative proofs.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When doubts about the truth of the Qur'an come to your mind—whether from whispers of shaytan or from modern arguments—do you have the tools from this lesson to rationally eliminate every alternative? Which alternative do you personally struggle with most, and how will you actively use Buti's proof to silence it?
?
You now know that the Prophet's revelation is not a matter of blind faith but rational certainty. Are you living with that conviction? Think of one area where you treat your belief in prophethood as mere tradition rather than certain knowledge. What will you do today to translate that certainty into action?
?
Buti says we are compelled to accept that the Prophet did not lie. Have you ever considered that if he had lied, he would have been the greatest liar in history, but the evidence of his truthfulness is overwhelming? How does that realization change the way you read his commands and prohibitions? Write down one command of the Prophet you find hard to follow, and tell yourself: 'I am certain he did not lie, so this command is from Allah.'

From Historical Reports to Rational Investigation of Revelation
Buti describes how investigating the Quran and the messenger raises the question of revelation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the verified reports about the Prophet Muhammad and the Quran lead to a rational investigation of the nature of revelation, distinct from historical or empirical inquiry.

Core Idea
The reliability of the Quran and the Prophet's claim forces a rational investigation into revelation.

Buti has just shown that the two reports—the historical account of Muhammad and the textual transmission of the Quran—are so reliable that falsehood is impossible. Now he takes the next step: the Prophet himself claimed the Quran is revelation. This claim raises a new question that cannot be answered by history or science alone. It demands a rational inquiry into what revelation truly is.

Guided Path
1
Recognize the two reliable reports
Begin by noting that Buti refers to two reports: one about the person of Muhammad (peace be upon him) and one about the Quran being revealed. Both are established as authentic and beyond doubt.
This sets the foundation: we are building on certain knowledge.
2
Identify the Prophet's claim
The Prophet stated that the Quran is not his own work but revelation from Allah through Jibril. This claim is part of the second report and is itself reliable.
The claim is not a separate speculation; it's transmitted as fact.
3
Understand the nature of the new question
Buti explains that investigating the phenomenon of revelation is different from verifying historical or physical facts. It is a rational issue, not a matter of narration or experiment.
This shifts the methodology from textual criticism to rational proof.
4
Learn the correct method for rational inquiry
The method for such a rational issue is 'clear entailment' (al-luzum al-bayyin) and 'certain primary analogical reasoning' (al-qiyas al-yaqini al-awwali) based on complete induction.
This prepares the reader for the upcoming argumentation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
لا يخضع لإمكان الكذب في روايته عن رجل اسمه محمد بن عبد الله ما ظهر في غضون القرن السادس الميلادي في الجزيرة العربية. كما نعلم لدى التحقيق في ذلك أيضاً بأن الرواية الصحيحة المتواترة أثبتت أنه كان يقول بأن هذا الكتاب ليس تأليفه وليس له كسب في شيء منه، وإنما هو يتلقاه وحياً من الله بواسطة من جبريل عليه السلام!.. فإذا انتهينا من تحقيق كل من هذين الخبرين، وجدنا أنفسنا أمام مسألة علمية أخرى هي ظاهرة هذا الوحي الذي أخبر عنه محمد صلى الله عليه وسلم فما هي حقيقته؟ وما الفرق بينه وبين الإلهام النفسي؟ وما مدى الاحتمالات العقلية للكذب في هذه الدعوى؟ فهذه قضية علمية أخرى ليست نقلاً حتى يكون تحقيقه عن طريق الرواية والسند، وليست حقيقة مادية محسوسة حتى يكون تحقيقها عن طريق التجربة المحسوسة المشاهدة، وإنما هي من قبيل القضايا العقلية المجردة، فليس من سبيل للتحقيق في أمرها إلا سبيل برهاني اللزوم البين والقياس اليقيني الأولى القائمين على الاستقراء التام.
It is not subject to the possibility of falsehood in its narration about a man named Muhammad ibn Abdullah who appeared during the sixth century CE in Arabia. And we also know, through investigation of that, that the authentic mutawatir narration proved that he used to say that this book is not his authorship and he has no earning in anything of it, but rather he receives it as revelation from Allah through the intermediary of Jibril (peace be upon him). So when we complete the investigation of each of these two reports, we find ourselves before another scientific issue, which is the phenomenon of this revelation that Muhammad (peace and blessings be upon him) reported. So what is its reality? And what is the difference between it and psychological inspiration? And what is the extent of the rational possibilities of falsehood in this claim? So this is another scientific issue that is not a transmitted report so that its verification would be through narration and chain, nor is it a material sensible reality so that its verification would be through sensory observed experiment, but rather it is of the type of abstract rational issues. So there is no way to investigate it except through the demonstrative path of clear entailment and certain primary analogical reasoning based on complete induction.
Source pages p. 105

Commentary
This passage establishes the groundwork for a rational investigation of prophetic revelation. Buti begins by noting that the report about Muhammad is so reliable that it cannot be subject to falsehood. Investigation shows that the Quran is claimed to be revelation. This leads to the core question: what is revelation? Buti classifies this as a rational issue, not a historical or empirical one. Therefore, it must be studied through logical deduction, entailment, and induction.

Key Terms
الوحي (revelation)
الرواية المتواترة (mutawatir narration)
القضايا العقلية (rational issues)
اللزوم البين (clear entailment)
الاستقراء التام (complete induction)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Revelation is merely a psychological or spiritual feeling that can be studied empirically.
Correction: Buti insists revelation is an abstract rational issue, not a sensory or emotional phenomenon, so it requires rational proof, not psychological observation.

Checkpoint
According to Buti, what type of issue is the phenomenon of revelation?
A) A transmitted historical issue
B) An empirical experimental issue
C) An abstract rational issue
D) A purely emotional issue

Key Takeaway
The investigation of revelation is a rational inquiry that depends on clear entailment and inductive reasoning, not on historical transmission or empirical observation.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You have likely accepted the Quran as revelation your whole life. But have you ever personally examined the rational grounds for that belief as Buti demands? If not, what prevents you—fear of doubt, laziness, or something else? Can you today commit to honestly investigating the claim of the Prophet using the rational method Buti outlines?
?
When you encounter a claim in deen, do you habitually ask whether it belongs to the category of transmitted reports, empirical facts, or rational issues? This lesson forces you to classify. What current belief are you holding in a category that Buti would say requires a different method of verification? Will you re-examine it?
?
Buti says the investigation of revelation is not simply about accepting or rejecting a report—it's a rational inquiry that demands your full intellectual engagement. Are you content to rely on inherited belief without doing this rational work yourself? What will you lose if you continue that way?
