ثانياً - الجان .
ثالثاً - الملائكة
رابعاً - قانون السببية في الكون .
Introduction
And by al-kawniyyat we mean everything that is known with certainty and conviction concerning the state of existing things, regarding which Allah, Mighty and Majestic, has commanded knowledge and belief in its existence.
And existing things include: humans, jinn, angels, and the rest of the creatures and other components such as heavens, orbs, earth, and seas, encompassing all that entails of causes, effects, and various cosmic motions.
And all these things are given the name: al-mukawwan (the made thing) or al-kawn (the cosmos).
And thereby you know that we do not intend by the word 'al-kawn' the meaning that some of those who speak about civilization intend when they divide existing things into three elements: the cosmos, humanity, and life. For they mean by the cosmos everything other than humanity and life from the rest of the other components, both living and inanimate.
And we do not see any linguistic justification for restricting 'al-kawn' to this extent of meaning, given what is known that it is in reality synonymous with the word 'al-wujud (existence)', so it ought to encompass everything that is called existing.
And on this basis, the researches of this section will include the study of realities related to the following:
First: Humans.
Second: Jinn.
Third: Angels.
Fourth: The law of causality in the cosmos.
Source pages p. 242

Commentary
This passage is an introduction where the author defines the term 'al-kawniyyat' (cosmic realities) and clarifies the scope of his book. The author begins by stating what he means by 'al-kawniyyat': everything that is known with certainty and conviction concerning the state of existing things that Allah has commanded us to know and believe in. He then specifies that 'existing things' (al-mawjudat) include humans, jinn, angels, and all other creatures and components such as heavens, orbs, earth, seas, and all causes, effects, and cosmic motions. All of these are called 'al-mukawwan' or 'al-kawn'. The author then contrasts his usage with a narrower definition used by some civilization theorists who divide existence into three elements: cosmos, humanity, and life. According to them, 'cosmos' excludes humans and life. The author rejects this narrowing as having no linguistic justification, arguing that the word 'al-kawn' is synonymous with 'al-wujud' (existence) and should encompass everything that exists. Therefore, the book's researches will include four topics: humans, jinn, angels, and the law of causality in the cosmos. This sets the stage for the subsequent discussions of these realities.

Key Terms
الكونيات
الموجودات
الكون
المكوّن
الوجود
قانون السببية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some restrict 'al-kawn' to exclude humans and life, limiting it to the non-human, non-living universe.
Correction: The author argues that 'al-kawn' is synonymous with 'existence' and should include all existents, including humans and life.

Checkpoint
According to the author, what does the term 'al-kawniyyat' refer to?
A) Everything that exists except humans and life.
B) Everything known with certainty about existing things that Allah commanded us to know and believe.
C) Only the physical universe like stars and planets.
D) Only angels and jinn.

Key Takeaway
Al-kawniyyat is defined as everything known with certainty about all existents, encompassing humans, jinn, angels, and the law of causality.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The author says Allah has commanded us to know and believe in the existence of all existents, including jinn and angels. Do you truly affirm their reality in your daily life, or do you live as if only the physical world is real? What would change if you acted on that belief right now?
?
The author rejects the narrow definition of 'cosmos' used by civilization theorists. Have you unconsciously adopted a worldview that excludes spiritual realities from your understanding of existence? How can you realign your perspective with the comprehensive Islamic view starting today?
?
One of the four topics is the law of causality. Do you attribute events in your life to mere chance or secondary causes, forgetting that Allah is the ultimate Cause? Commit to reflecting on one event this week where you will consciously trace the causality back to Allah's will.

Defining al-Kawniyyat: Scope and Subjects of Study
Author defines al-kawniyyat and outlines study topics.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the author's definition of al-kawniyyat and the specific topics that will be studied in this section.

Core Idea
Al-kawn means all existence, not just the physical universe.

In this opening passage, the author sets the stage by defining what he means by 'al-kawniyyat' (cosmic realities). He clarifies that his usage aligns with the full scope of existence, contrasting with a common restricted meaning. He then lists the four main subjects of study: humans, jinn, angels, and the law of causality, emphasizing that only those truths with religious obligation are within the book's scope.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its English translation to grasp the author's definition of 'al-kawniyyat' and note the examples he gives.
Pay attention to the contrast he makes with a secular definition.
2
Contrast two definitions
Identify how the author's definition of 'al-kawn' differs from the common secular definition that restricts it to the physical universe excluding humans and life.
The author argues linguistically for a synonymous relationship with 'existence'.
3
List the four topics
Find the enumerated list of topics that will be studied: humans, jinn, angels, and the law of causality.
These are not all possible truths, but those with religious obligation.
4
Understand the scope restriction
Notice the author's statement that only truths which Allah commanded us to know and believe are included; other factual details are merely permissible to research.
This sets the methodological boundary of the book.

فلا جرم أن لا شأن لنا بما وراء ذلك من الحقائق الأخرى المتعلقة بطبائع بعض الأشياء وتركيبها واكتشاف المجهول منها . إذ لا يتعلق بها أي حكم ديني أكثر من مشروعية البحث فيها ومحاولة الاكتشاف لها
✩
محمد
Preamble. By 'al-kawniyyat' (cosmic realities) we mean everything known with certainty and certitude concerning existing things, which Allah, Mighty and Majestic, has commanded us to know and believe in their existence. Existing things include: humans, jinn, angels, and all other created beings and components such as heavens, spheres, earth, and seas, including whatever that entails of causes, effects, and various cosmic movements. All these things are called 'al-mukawwan' (the created) or 'al-kawn' (the cosmos). By this you know that we do not intend by the word 'al-kawn' the meaning that some who discuss civilization intend when they divide existing things into three elements: the cosmos, humanity, and life. They mean by 'al-kawn' everything other than humanity and life from the rest of the other components, living and non-living. We do not see any linguistic justification for restricting 'al-kawn' to this measure of meaning, despite what is known that it is in reality synonymous with the word 'al-wujud' (existence), so it should include everything called existent. On this basis, the researches of this section will include the study of truths related to the following: First: humans. Second: jinn. Third: angels. Fourth: the law of causality in the cosmos. And as I told you, what concerns us from the truths of these existing things is only that which Allah, Mighty and Majestic, has charged us with knowing, then believing in, and holding conviction according to it. So it is no wonder that we have no concern with what lies beyond that of other truths related to the natures of some things, their composition, and the discovery of what is unknown about them, since no religious ruling attaches to them beyond the permissibility of researching them and attempting to discover them.
✩
Muhammad
Source pages p. 243

Commentary
This passage is an introduction that defines the scope and subject matter of the book. The author begins by defining 'al-kawniyyat' (cosmic realities) as certain knowledge about existents that Allah has commanded us to know and believe in. He then lists the categories of existents: humans, jinn, angels, and all other creations including heavens, earth, seas, and their causes and movements. He emphasizes that all these are called 'al-kawn' or 'al-mukawwan'. Next, he clarifies that his usage of 'al-kawn' differs from a common secular definition that restricts it to the physical universe excluding humans and life; he argues linguistically that 'al-kawn' is synonymous with 'existence' and should include everything that exists. Following this, he enumerates the four specific topics that will be studied in this section: humans, jinn, angels, and the law of causality. Finally, he states that the book will only address those truths that carry religious obligation—belief in them is commanded—and not other factual details about the natures and compositions of things, which are merely permissible to research but not obligatory.

الموجودات

القانون

Correction: The author clarifies that 'al-kawn' is synonymous with 'existence' and includes humans, jinn, angels, and all creations.

Key Takeaway
The term 'al-kawn' encompasses all of existence, and this book focuses only on those truths that carry religious obligation.

?

What would change if you saw every existent as something Allah commands you to believe in?

Avoiding Speculation about Adam's Descent from Paradise
Buti warns against unnecessary inquiry into Adam's descent and multiplication

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Buti considers details of Adam's descent to be outside the scope of obligatory creed and why engaging in such speculation is considered superfluous.

Core Idea
Not every historical detail is required belief. Only what has definitive proof matters for creed.

In this passage, Buti addresses a common tendency to delve into specifics about Adam's descent from Paradise and the multiplication of his progeny. He establishes a key methodological principle: theological inquiry must be limited to matters for which there is definitive evidence from the Quran and Sunnah. This lesson explains his reasoning and its implications for the study of creed.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and its translation
Begin by reading the Arabic original and its English translation to grasp the general meaning. Note the key phrases: 'la shan lana', 'fudul al-nazar wa al-qawl', and 'la dalil qati'.
2
Identify Buti's methodological claim
Buti states that researching the 'how' of Adam's descent and multiplication is not relevant to creed ('la madkhal lahu bi-amr al-‘aqida'). Understand that he is not dismissing these events as unimportant, but restricting theological obligation.
3
Recognize the criterion for creedal beliefs
Buti implies that only beliefs backed by definitive evidence ('dalil qati‘ min kitab aw sunna') are obligatory. Speculation without proof is superfluous. Reflect on how this principle protects the purity of Islamic creed.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
واعلم أنه لاشأن لنا في هذا المقام بالبحث في كيفية نزول آدم من الجنة ، والتحقيق في البقعة التي هبط إليها من الأرض ، وكيفية تكاثر النسل من آدم وحواء بعد ذلك . إذ كل ذلك مما لامدخل لـه بـأمر العقيدة القائمة على الأحكام الثابتة القطعية بل الحديث في ذلك كله من فضول النظر والقول ، ولا يوجد دليل قاطع على شيء من ذلك في كتاب أو سنة ، ولذلك لم يتعبـدنـا الله عز وجل باعتقاد شيء معين فيه
Know that we have no concern in this context with researching how Adam descended from Paradise, investigating the spot on earth to which he descended, and how progeny multiplied from Adam and Eve after that. For all that is something that has no entry into the matter of creed based on definitive rulings. Rather, all discussion about that is from superfluous consideration and speech, and there is no definitive evidence for anything of that in the Book or the Sunnah, and therefore God Almighty did not obligate us to believe any specific thing about it.
Source pages p. 250

Commentary
This passage establishes a methodological principle: details of Adam's descent from Paradise, the location, and the process of multiplication are not required beliefs (aqida). They lack definitive proof in Quran or Sunnah, so Muslims are not obligated to hold any specific view. Engaging in such debates is considered 'superfluous consideration and speech' (fudul al-nazar wa al-qawl).

Correction: Buti clarifies that only matters with definitive evidence are obligatory beliefs. Details of Adam's descent lack such proof, so Muslims are not required to hold specific views.

Key Takeaway

Limits of Inquiry on Adam and Refutation of Speculative Claims
Warning and refutation regarding Adam's descent and speculative claims

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why details of Adam's descent and multiplication are not part of creed, and how to refute claims of earlier Adams and alleged contradictions in the Quran.

Core Idea
Not every question about the unseen is answerable; creed is built on definitive proofs, not speculation.

In this passage, the author sets clear boundaries for theological inquiry. He warns against delving into unwarranted details about Adam's descent and the multiplication of offspring, as these are not established by definitive evidence. He then refutes two erroneous claims: the Sufi notion of earlier Adams and the atheist charge of contradiction in the Quran's descriptions of human creation. This lesson will help you understand the proper approach to such topics.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage
Read the Arabic passage once without analysis. Then read the translation to grasp the full argument.
Notice the strong warnings: 'لا شأن لنا' and 'إياك أن تلتفت'.
2
Identify the three parts
The passage has three main parts: (1) warning about investigating details of Adam, (2) refutation of earlier Adams claim, (3) refutation of contradiction claim and the methodological principle.
Each part serves a distinct purpose.
3
Analyze the methodology
Reflect on the principle: matters of creed require definitive proof; speculation ('فضول النظر') is not permissible. Why does the author call it surplus speech?
This is a key methodological point in Islamic theology.
4
Refute the misconceptions
See how the author refutes the Sufi claim as 'حدس مجرد' (pure conjecture) and the atheist claim as a misunderstanding of linguistic specification.
The analogy of building materials clarifies the alleged contradiction.
5
Apply the principle
Apply the principle: for unseen matters, we rely on revelation; for empirical matters, we use observation. How does this guide your approach to similar questions?

واعلم أنه لاشأن لنا في هذا المقام بالبحث في كيفية نزول آدم من الجنة ، والتحقيق في البقعة التي هبط إليها من الأرض ، وكيفية تكاثر النسل من آدم وحواء بعد ذلك . إذ كل ذلك مما لامدخل لـه بـأمر العقيدة القائمة على الأحكام الثابتة القطعية بل الحديث في ذلك كله من فضول النظر والقول ، ولا يوجد دليل قاطع على شيء من ذلك في كتاب أو سنة ، ولذلك لم يتعبـدنـا الله عز وجل باعتقاد شيء معين فيه
وإياك أن تلتفت إلى ما يقوله بعض المتصوفة ، من زعم أن آدم عليه الصلاة والسلام المذكور قصة خلقه في القرآن - كان مسبوقاً بأوادم كثيرين غيره . ثم يذهبون يجرون ذيل الخيال في تفصيل الحديث عن ذلك
فهذا الادعاء مبني على الحدس المجرد ، لا يدعمه دليل من الخبر الصادق القطعي ولا برهان يقيني من النظر العلمي . ومن الأدب مع كتاب الله تعالى
(1) من العجيب المضحك أن بعض الملاحدة أرادوا أن يزعموا أن في القرآن تناقضاً ، فعكفوا على البحث عن ذلك .. ثم اهتدوا إلى هذا التناقض في هذا الذي يقوله عن أصل الإنسان : مرة يقول إنه مخلوق من تراب ، ومرة من صلصال ، ومرة من حمأ مسنون كالتناقض الذي يقع فيه من يقول : إن هذا البيت مبني من تراب من طين من آجر ! .. وإذا فقد الإنسان حريته حتى أصبحت ملك سادته ، فلا عجب أن يفقد عقله أيضاً ، فيفكر وهو برغبة غيره .
وسنة رسوله أن نكل علم مالم يبينه الله عز وجل ولا رسوله إلى علم الله وحده اللهم إلا ماكان من ذلك خاضعاً لوسائل البحث والتجربة والمشاهدة ، فقد دعـانـا كلام الله تعالى إلى البحث عن الحقيقة والتنقيب عن اليقين في ذلك ج
And know that we have no concern in this context with investigating the manner of Adam's descent from Paradise, and determining the specific spot on earth to which he descended, and the manner of the multiplication of offspring from Adam and Eve thereafter. For all of that has no bearing on the matter of creed, which is based upon definitive rulings. Rather, discourse about all of that is from surplus speculation and speech, and there is no definitive proof for anything of that in the Book or the Sunnah, and therefore God Almighty did not obligate us to believe anything specific concerning it.
And beware of paying attention to what some Sufis say, claiming that the Adam mentioned in the story of his creation in the Quran was preceded by many other Adams. Then they go on dragging the tail of imagination in detailing speech about that.
This claim is based on pure conjecture, supported neither by a definitive truthful report nor by a certain proof from scientific reasoning. And from proper etiquette with the Book of God Almighty and the Sunnah of His Messenger is that we consign knowledge of what God Almighty and His Messenger have not made clear to God alone, except for that which is subject to the means of research, experiment, and observation; for the speech of God Almighty has called us to search for truth and to dig for certainty in that.
Source pages p. 250

Commentary
This passage serves as a methodological warning against delving into speculative details about Adam's descent and multiplication, and it refutes two erroneous claims: (1) the claim of some Sufis about earlier Adams, and (2) the atheist claim of contradiction in the Quranic descriptions of human creation. The author begins by stating that investigating how Adam descended from Paradise, where exactly he landed, and how offspring multiplied from Adam and Eve is not part of the creed because these details are not established by definitive evidence from Quran or Sunnah. God has not obligated belief in any specific view on these matters. Then he warns against Sufi claims of earlier Adams, calling them pure conjecture without support. Finally, he addresses atheist accusations of contradiction, showing that the different terms (dust, clay, mud) are not contradictions but progressive specifications, just as saying a house is built of dust, then clay, then brick is not contradictory. He then reiterates the principle: for matters of the unseen, we rely on revelation; only that which is subject to empirical research can be investigated by reason.

The Necessity of Comprehensive Induction: Including Revelation as a Hypothesis
Buti critiques the exclusion of revelation and advocates comprehensive induction.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the methodological flaw of excluding divine revelation from investigations about origins, and the principle of comprehensive induction that considers all possibilities without bias.

Core Idea
Excluding a possibility from the start is not science; it is an intellectual prison.

In this passage, Buti addresses a common objection: if evolutionist theories are flawed, why do they still accept the general idea? His answer exposes a methodological bias—they have already ruled out the possibility that revelation might hold the truth. This sets up a contrast between a limited, relative logic and the comprehensive induction that all rational inquiry should follow.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection and answer
Read the Arabic passage once, then the translation. Notice how Buti poses the question and then gives a detailed answer.
The objection is from an imagined interlocutor; the answer is Buti's main argument.
2
Identify the excluded possibility
Find where Buti says the researchers discarded a key possibility. What is that possibility, and why did they discard it?
The possibility is that the truth might be as explained by the Creator in revelation.
3
Understand the 'relative logic'
Buti describes the researchers' reasoning as logical within their self-imposed prison. Consider why he calls it 'relative logic' and why it is incomplete.
Relative logic is valid only within a narrow framework that excludes certain options.
4
Contrast with comprehensive induction
Buti presents his own method: comprehensive induction that includes all initial possibilities. Compare the two approaches and note the role of desire, environment, and utility.
Comprehensive induction means placing all possibilities under one microscope without excluding any a priori.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
غير أنك قد تسأل : فإذا كان الأمر هكذا فما للباحثين والناقدين أنفسهم يعودون فيقبلون فكرة النشوء والارتقاء في الجملة ، أي بقطع النظر عن اتباع مذهب معين من المذاهب التي عرضنا لها ؟ والجواب ، أن هؤلاء الباحثين لم يضعوا في بداية بحثهم جميع الاحتمالات الموضوعية المتعلقة بهذه المسألة تحت مجهر واحد من النظر والفحص ، فقد نبـذوا من احتمالات الأمر ما لا رغبة لهم فيه ولم يقفوا عنده بأي تأمل أو نظر ، ألا وهو احتمال أن تكون الحقيقة كما قد فسرها خالق الكون نفسه في كتابه المنزل على خاتم أنبيائه عليه الصلاة والسلام . ثم حصروا أنفسهم في الحلقة التي انطبقت عليهم أو في نهاية الطريق الذي سدوه على أنفسهم . وضمن هذا النطاق المحصور راحوا يبحثون ويتساءلون عن النشأة الأولى وأصل الخلق وعلاقة الإنسان بالحيوانات الأخرى . فكان عليهم ـ وقد حكموا على أنفسهم بهذا السجن الفكري ـ أن يتخيروا أقرب الحلول والأجوبة التي يجدونها أمامهم ، فإذا لم يعثروا على الأقرب فإن عليهم - على كل حال ـ أن لا يرجعوا من بحوثهم بأفكار فارغة ، إذ إن الرجوع بافتراض ما - مهما كان محاطاً بالريب والشكوك - أليق بطموح الفكر والعقل من الرجوع بموقف سلبي حائر . وهكذا فإن قبول أي مذهب يفترض فكرة التطور في حياة الإنسان والحيوانات الأخرى ، مهما كان فيه من النقائض والثغرات ، أقرب إلى الفكر العلمي من القول بأن الأرض أو السماء انشقت فجأة عن كائن معقد الصنع عجيب الطوية ، يهدد الأرض بقوته ويطمح إلى القمر والنجوم بسلطـانـه . وهو إن لم يقبل ذاك لا بد أن يجد عقله مرغماً على قبول هذا . ومن منا يتردد في اختيار الحل الأول ، على علاته ، عندما نجد أنفسنا محصورين في مضيق ليس فيه إلاّ أحد هذين الحلين؟ ولا ريب أن هذا الاختيار يستند إلى منطق ! .. ولكنه منطق نسبي ينسجم مع عقلية ذاك الذي وضع نفسه في حلقة مقفلة أو حصر فكره في طريق مسدود ، ومن ثم فهو يعد منطقياً وصادقاً مع نفسه عنـدمـا يقول وهو في محبسه ذاك : هذا كل ما أراه أمامي فهل للعقل من سبيل إلا أن يتخير أقرب الحلول؟ غير أنه جهل عظيم وانخداع خطير أمام مقياس الاستقراء التام ، والانطلاق في دنيا الحقيقة كلها ، بكل احتمالاتها الواردة ، دون تحكيم للرغبة ولا للبيئة ولا للتقاليد ولا لسلطان المنفعة . أما نحن ، وقد التزمنا في بحوثنا ودراساتنا العلمية ، مبدأ الاستقراء وسبر الاحتمالات والفروض كلها ، ووضعها جميعاً تحت مجهر واحد من النظر والبحث : فإن علينا أن نضع في اعتبارنا جميع ما يتعلق بهذا الموضوع من احتمالات مبدئية ، بما فيها تقرير الخالق جل جلاله المتضمن تفسير هذا الأمر .
However, you may ask: If the matter is so, why do the researchers and critics themselves go back and accept the idea of evolution in general, i.e., regardless of following a particular doctrine among the doctrines we have presented? The answer: These researchers did not, at the beginning of their investigation, place all the objective possibilities related to this issue under a single microscope of examination and scrutiny; rather, they discarded those possibilities they had no desire for and did not stop at them with any reflection or consideration, namely the possibility that the truth might be as the Creator of the universe Himself has explained it in His Book revealed to the Seal of His Prophets, peace be upon him. Then they confined themselves to the circle that applied to them or to the end of the path they blocked for themselves. Within this limited scope, they began to search and inquire about the first origin and the origin of creation and the relationship of man with other animals. So it was incumbent upon them—having sentenced themselves to this intellectual prison—to choose the closest solutions and answers they found before them. If they did not find the closest, then they had, in any case, not to return from their researches with empty ideas, for returning with a hypothesis—no matter how surrounded by doubt and uncertainty—is more befitting to the ambition of thought and mind than returning with a negative, bewildered stance. Thus, accepting any doctrine that assumes the idea of evolution in the life of man and other animals, no matter what defects and gaps it contains, is closer to scientific thought than saying that the earth or sky suddenly split open into a complexly constructed being of wonderful disposition, threatening the earth with its power and aspiring to the moon and stars with its authority. And if he does not accept that, his mind inevitably finds itself compelled to accept this. And who among us hesitates in choosing the first solution, with all its faults, when we find ourselves in a strait where there is no solution but one of these two? No doubt this choice is based on logic!... But it is a relative logic that harmonizes with the mentality of one who has placed himself in a closed circle or confined his thought to a dead end, and therefore he is considered logical and honest with himself when he says in his prison: 'This is all I see before me; does the mind have any way but to choose the closest solution?' However, it is great ignorance and dangerous deception measured against the standard of comprehensive induction and launching into the entire realm of truth, with all its probable possibilities, without imposing desire, environment, traditions, or the authority of utility. As for us, having committed ourselves in our scientific researches and studies to the principle of induction and probing all possibilities and hypotheses, and placing them all under a single microscope of examination and research: we must take into consideration all the initial possibilities related to this subject, including the statement of the Creator, Glorified is He, containing the explanation of this matter.
Source pages p. 267

Commentary
This passage is an objection-and-answer followed by a methodological declaration. The author poses an objection: if the evolutionists' detailed theories are so flawed, why do they nonetheless accept the general idea of evolution? The answer is that these researchers began their inquiry by excluding a key possibility from the start: the possibility that the truth about origins might be as described by the Creator in revelation. They confined themselves to naturalistic explanations, thus creating an intellectual prison. Within that prison, they must choose the least problematic naturalistic hypothesis rather than admit ignorance. The author describes their logic as 'relative logic'—valid only within their self-imposed limitations, but not comprehensive. He contrasts this with his own methodology: comprehensive induction that includes all possibilities, including divine revelation, without bias. The passage thus defends the necessity of considering the revealed explanation as a legitimate hypothesis in any rational inquiry.

Key Terms
فكرة النشوء والارتقاء
الاستقراء التام
احتمالات مبدئية
منطق نسبي
سجن فكري
تقرير الخالق

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The author is rejecting all scientific reasoning and empirical investigation.
Correction: Buti is not rejecting science; he is critiquing the arbitrary exclusion of a valid hypothesis (revelation) from the start. He advocates for a comprehensive approach that includes all possibilities, including the revealed explanation.

Checkpoint
What methodological flaw does the author identify in those who accept the general idea of evolution while rejecting detailed theories?
A) They ignore all empirical evidence.
B) They exclude the possibility of divine revelation from the outset.
C) They rely on outdated scientific data.
D) They are biased toward religious explanations.

Key Takeaway
Comprehensive induction requires that no legitimate hypothesis, including divine revelation, be excluded from the start.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
In which area of your life have you confined yourself to only 'naturalistic' explanations, refusing to consider that God might have a say? What would it cost you to open that door?
?
Are you more afraid of not having an answer than of having the wrong one? How does that fear keep you from seeking the truth from its full source, including revelation?
?
You claim to seek truth, but have you honestly placed God's revelation under the same microscope as your own opinions? Or have you already decided which hypothesis is acceptable before you began?

Method of Learning
intermediate
6 min
The False Dilemma of Evolution vs. Creation
Buti critiques the false dilemma between evolution and special creation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Buti exposes the flawed logic of the forced choice between evolution and special creation, and identifies it as relative logic confined to a closed system.

Core Idea
Choosing evolution over creation can be relative logic, not true science.

Buti begins by describing a common intellectual trap: believing there are only two options—evolution or a miraculous special creation. Within that narrow frame, choosing evolution seems logical. Buti calls this 'relative logic' and warns that it ignores the full landscape of possibilities. This lesson examines his critique and the concept of relative logic.

Guided Path
1
Read the Passage
Read the Arabic passage and its translation carefully, focusing on the first part where Buti describes the predicament of the one who limits options.
2
Identify the False Dilemma
Notice how Buti frames the choice: either accept evolution with its flaws or accept a sudden miraculous creation. He argues this is a constrained perspective.
This is a common rhetorical move.
3
Understand Relative Logic
Buti introduces the idea of 'relative logic'—a logic that seems sound within a closed system but is flawed when considering all possibilities. Reflect on what makes it relative.
Relative logic is tied to the environment, desire, or limited data.
4
Reflect on the Limitations
Consider why Buti calls this approach 'great ignorance and dangerous deception' and how it fails the standard of comprehensive induction.
This connects to the next lesson's methodology.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ما - مهما كان محاطاً بالريب والشكوك - أليق بطموح الفكر والعقل من الرجوع بموقف سلبي حائر . وهكذا فإن قبول أي مذهب يفترض فكرة التطور في حياة الإنسان والحيوانات الأخرى ، مهما كان فيه من النقائض والثغرات ، أقرب إلى الفكر العلمي من القول بأن الأرض أو السماء انشقت فجأة عن كائن معقد الصنع عجيب الطوية ، يهدد الأرض بقوته ويطمح إلى القمر والنجوم بسلطانه . وهو إن لم يقبل ذاك لا بد أن يجد عقله مرغماً على قبول هذا . ومن منا يتردد في اختيار الحل الأول ، على علاته ، عندما نجد أنفسنا محصورين في مضيق ليس فيه إلاّ أحد هذين الحلين . ولا ريب أن هذا الاختيار يستند إلى منطق ! .. ولكنه منطق نسبي ينسجم مع عقلية ذاك الذي وضع نفسه في حلقة مقفلة أو حصر فكره في طريق مسدود ، ومن ثم فهو يعد منطقياً وصادقاً مع نفسه عندما يقول وهو في محبسه ذاك : هذا كل ما أراه أمامي فهل للعقل من سبيل إلا أن يتخير أقرب الحلول غير أنه جهل عظيم وانخداع خطير أمام مقياس الاستقراء التام ، والانطلاق في دنيا الحقيقة كلها ، بكل احتمالاتها الواردة ، دون تحكيم للرغبة ولا للبيئة ولا للتقاليد ولا لسلطان المنفعة . أما نحن ، وقد التزمنا في بحوثنا ودراساتنا العلمية ، مبدأ الاستقراء وسبر الاحتمالات والفروض كلها ، ووضعها جميعاً تحت مجهر واحد من النظر والبحث : فإن علينا أن نضع في اعتبارنا جميع ما يتعلق بهذا الموضوع من احتمالات مبدئية ، بما فيها تقرير الخالق جل جلاله المتضمن تفسير هذا الأمر . وقد استعرضنا الاحتمالات التي افترضها أصحاب فكرة النشوء والارتقاء ، فرأيناها جميعاً تعاني من وطأة انتقادات هامة وجهت إليها ، ورأينا كلاً منها يصرع الآخر ويبطله ، كما قد رأيت في استعراضنا السريع . علينا إذاً أن نلتفت فنصغي إلى تقرير الخالق ذاته ، وهو يحدثنا عن تفصيل الأمر وحقيقته . وكنا قد انتهينا في دراساتنا السابقة إلى اليقين التام بوجود الله تعالى يقيناً يستند إلى مختلف الأدلة العلمية القاطعة ، وإلى اليقين ببعثة الأنبياء والرسل بما فيهم خاتم الأنبياء محمد عليه الصلاة والسلام ، وبالكتب المنزلة وحياً عليهم ، كل ذلك بالأدلة المنطقية العلمية التي تم شرحها في أماكنها - فرأينا الخالق جل جلاله يقرر بأنه خلق الإنسان في أحسن تقويم ، وأنه تكاثر من نسل أبيه آدم الذي خلقه الله وبث فيه الإدراك وعلمه البيان والتعبير عن الأشياء بما ألهمه من أسمائها . ثم رأيناه يتحدث في بيانه هذا عن هؤلاء المتخاصمين حول كيفية نشأتهم والتفسير الذي يجب أن يعتمدوه لما قد تخيلوه من فرضية تطور الإنسان ، وقد أصموا آذانهم عن بيان الخالق نفسه للأمر ـ رأيناه يتحدث عنهم بأسلوب يشع بالرهبة وجلال الربوبية ، قائلاً { ما أشهدتهم خلق السموات والأرض ولا خلق أنفسهم وما كنت متخذ المضلين عضداً } [ الكهف : ٥١ ] . هكذا بحثنا واستقصينا . فبأي الاحتمالات نؤمن ونصدق ؟ أنغمض العين والفكر ونؤمن بواحد من تلك المذاهب السالف ذكرها على ما تعانيه من ثغرات وترزح تحته انتقادات ونحمل العقل كرهاً على افتراضه ثم التصديق به . أم من نؤمن بتقرير الخالق نفسه بعد أن آمنا به وفرغنا من الإيمان برسله وكتبه وقرآنه ؟ لا يتردد العاقل الحر لحظة واحدة في أن علينا - بعد إيماننا بالله ورسله وكتبه - أن نطرح اضطراب المضطربين وحيرة المحتارين جانباً . ثم نصدق الخبر الصادق الثابت الواصل إلينا بطريق القطع والتواتر . نقول هذا كله عن قصة خلق الإنسان التي ورد شرحها في كلام الله عز وجل بعبارة صريحة قاطعة لا تحتمل لبساً ولا تأويلاً .
What - no matter how surrounded by doubt and suspicion - is more befitting to the aspiration of thought and intellect than retreating with a negative bewildered stance? Thus, accepting any doctrine that assumes the idea of evolution in the life of humans and other animals, no matter how many contradictions and gaps it contains, is closer to scientific thought than saying that the earth or the sky suddenly split open to reveal a being of complex construction, wondrous nature, threatening the earth with its power and aspiring to the moon and stars with its dominion. And if he does not accept that, he inevitably finds his mind compelled to accept this. And who among us hesitates to choose the first solution, with all its defects, when we find ourselves confined in a strait with no way out except one of these two solutions? There is no doubt that this choice is based on logic! ... But it is relative logic that harmonizes with the mentality of one who has placed himself in a closed loop or confined his thought to a dead end. Hence, he is considered logical and honest with himself when he says in that prison: 'This is all I see before me; is there any way for the intellect except to choose the closest solution?' However, it is great ignorance and dangerous deception when measured against the standard of complete induction, and launching into the entire world of reality, with all its possible probabilities, without the influence of desire, environment, traditions, or the authority of benefit. As for us, having committed in our scientific researches and studies to the principle of induction and exploring all probabilities and hypotheses, placing them all under one microscope of examination and research: we must take into consideration all the preliminary probabilities related to this subject, including the statement of the Creator, exalted be His majesty, which contains the explanation of this matter. And we have reviewed the probabilities assumed by the proponents of the idea of evolution, and we saw them all suffering from the weight of important criticisms directed at them, and we saw each one striking down the other and invalidating it, as you saw in our brief review. We must therefore turn and listen to the statement of the Creator Himself, as He tells us the detail of the matter and its truth. And we had concluded in our previous studies to complete certainty of the existence of Allah the Exalted, a certainty based on various definitive scientific proofs, and to certainty of the mission of the prophets and messengers including the seal of the prophets Muhammad, peace be upon him, and to the books revealed as revelation upon them, all of this by logical scientific proofs that were explained in their places. Then we saw the Creator, exalted be His majesty, declaring that He created man in the best stature, and that he multiplied from the seed of his father Adam, whom Allah created and instilled in him perception and taught him eloquence and expression of things by what He inspired him of their names. Then we saw Him speaking in this statement of His about those disputants regarding the manner of their origin and the interpretation they must adopt for what they had imagined of the hypothesis of human evolution, having blocked their ears from the statement of the Creator Himself about the matter — we saw Him speaking about them in a style radiating with awe and the majesty of divinity, saying: 'I did not make them witness to the creation of the heavens and the earth, nor to the creation of themselves, and I would not take the misleaders as assistants' [Surah al-Kahf: 51]. Thus we researched and investigated. So which of the probabilities do we believe and affirm? Do we close our eyes and minds and believe in one of those doctrines previously mentioned, with what gaps they suffer and under which criticisms they groan, and forcibly carry the mind to assume it then believe in it? Or do we believe in the statement of the Creator Himself after we have believed in Him and completed faith in His messengers, His books, and His Qur'an? The free rational person does not hesitate for a moment that we must - after our faith in Allah, His messengers, and His books - cast aside the confusion of the confused and the bewilderment of the bewildered. Then we believe the truthful, established report reaching us by the way of definitiveness and mass transmission. We say all this regarding the story of the creation of man, which is explained in the speech of Allah, mighty and majestic, in clear, definitive wording that admits no ambiguity or interpretation.
Source pages p. 268

Commentary
This passage presents a culminating argument in Buti's refutation of the theory of evolution and his affirmation of the Quranic account of creation. The author begins by characterizing the intellectual predicament of those who limit themselves to only two options: either accept evolution with all its flaws, or accept a literal 'special creation' event that seems miraculous. He notes that within that constrained framework, choosing evolution appears logical. However, Buti condemns this as 'relative logic' that operates within a closed loop or dead end, ignoring the full spectrum of possibilities. True scientific methodology, he insists, requires comprehensive induction (istiqra' tamm) that considers all hypotheses—including the possibility of divine revelation. He then recounts that his previous studies have established certainty of God's existence, prophethood, and the divine origin of scriptures through definitive proofs. With that foundation, the Quranic account of creation is not just one option among others; it is the authoritative statement of the Creator. The author quotes Quran 18:51 to show that the disbelievers were not present at creation, implying their theories are speculative. The rational person, after believing in Allah and His messengers, must prefer the definitive transmitted report (khabar qat'i mutawatir) over human conjecture. The passage ends by affirming that the Quranic narrative is explicit and admits no allegorical interpretation.

Key Terms
النشوء والارتقاء
تقرير الخالق

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That choosing evolution over special creation is a purely objective scientific decision.
Correction: Buti argues that this choice is often based on relative logic limited to a false dilemma, not on comprehensive induction of all possibilities.

Checkpoint
According to Buti, what is the main problem with the reasoning of those who choose evolution over special creation?
A) They ignore the principle of induction and do not consider all possible hypotheses, including divine revelation.
B) They are not logical at all.
C) They rely on miracles as explanations.
D) They reject science entirely.

Key Takeaway
Buti exposes the false dilemma between evolution and creation as a form of relative logic that fails the standard of comprehensive induction.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever felt forced to choose between two unattractive worldviews, only to realize later that you were ignoring a third option? What keeps you from seeking that third option now?
?
Buti warns that relative logic can make a flawed choice seem rational within a closed system. In what area of your life—your career, relationships, or faith—might you be operating in a 'closed loop' shaped by desire or environment rather than seeking the full truth?
?
The passage says true induction requires launching into 'the entire world of reality' without bias. Is there a truth about God or the unseen that you have been avoiding because it doesn't fit the limited options you've considered? What would it cost you to honestly consider it?

Method of Learning
intermediate

Comprehensive Induction and the Authority of Revelation
Buti advocates comprehensive induction and accepts the Quranic creation account as definitive.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Buti's argument that true scientific methodology requires considering all hypotheses, including divine revelation, and that after establishing faith, the Quranic account of creation must be accepted as definitive.

Core Idea
True science considers divine revelation as a valid hypothesis.

Having exposed the false dilemma, Buti now presents the correct methodology: comprehensive induction (istiqra' tamm) that examines all possibilities without bias. He then applies this to the question of human origins, reviewing evolutionary hypotheses and finding them wanting. Finally, he reminds the reader that previous studies have established certainty in God, prophets, and scriptures. With that foundation, the Quranic account is not merely one hypothesis but the authoritative truth from the Creator.

Guided Path
1
Read the Passage
Read the Arabic passage and translation from 'As for us...' to the end. Focus on Buti's methodological shift and his conclusion.
2
Understand Comprehensive Induction
Notice how Buti defines his own methodology: considering all preliminary probabilities, including the statement of the Creator. This is contrasted with the earlier relative logic.
Key term: الاستقراء التام (complete induction).
3
Review the Foundational Certainties
Buti references previous proofs for God's existence, prophethood, and scriptures. Identify how these certainties shape his approach to the creation debate.
This shows that the argument is not purely philosophical but rooted in established creed.
4
See the Quranic Proof
Buti quotes Quran 18:51 to emphasize that humans were not witnesses to their own creation, undermining speculative theories. Then he concludes that the rational person accepts the definitive transmitted report.
5
Reflect on the Conclusion
Consider why Buti insists the Quranic account is 'clear definitive wording that admits no ambiguity or interpretation' and how this settles the matter for a believer.

With that foundation, the Quranic account of creation is not just one option among others; it is the authoritative statement of the Creator. The author quotes Quran 18:51 to show that the disbelievers were not present at creation, implying their theories are speculative. The rational person, after believing in Allah and His messengers, must prefer the definitive transmitted report (khabar qat'i mutawatir) over human conjecture. The passage ends by affirming that the Quranic narrative is explicit and admits no allegorical interpretation.

Key Terms

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That scientific methodology must exclude divine revelation as a possible explanation.
Correction: Buti argues that true induction considers all possibilities, including revelation, and that rejecting it a priori is unscientific.

Key Takeaway
Comprehensive induction includes revelation, and after certainty in God and prophets, the Quranic creation account is the definitive truth.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

?

?

In what areas of your life are you acting as if you were a witness to creation, asserting your own reasoning over Allah's clear words? Will you repent and surrender to His definitive speech today?

Accepting the Creator's Account of Human Origins
Buti argues for accepting the Qur'anic account of human creation over evolutionary theory after certainty in revelation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that after establishing certainty in God, prophets, and scriptures, a Muslim must accept the Quranic account of human creation as the definitive truth over speculative theories.

Core Idea
When revelation speaks definitively, human theories must yield.

Buti has already built a solid foundation for certainty in God, prophets, and scriptures. Now he addresses the specific question of human origins. He insists that once these certainties are in place, the rational person must accept the clear Qur'anic account, not speculative theories. In this passage, he contrasts the flawed human hypotheses with the Creator's own decisive statement.

Guided Path
1
Recap the certainties
Remind yourself of the certainties Buti has established in earlier studies: the existence of God through definitive proofs, the truth of prophethood, and the divine origin of the revealed books.
These certainties form the basis for accepting the Creator's statement.
2
Contrast the accounts
Notice how Buti presents the Quranic account of human creation (Adam, best stature, perception) and contrasts it with the evolutionary hypothesis that he describes as filled with gaps and criticisms.
The Quranic account is clear and decisive; the human theories are full of problems.
3
Make the choice
Follow Buti's rhetorical question: do we believe in flawed human schools or the Creator's own report? He answers decisively: after faith in God, messengers, and books, we must set aside confusion and accept the definitive transmitted report (tawatur).
This is the key conclusion: revelation takes priority over speculation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
علينا إذاً أن نلتفت فنصغي إلى تقرير الخالق ذاته ، وهو يحدثنا عن تفصيل الأمر وحقيقته . - وكنا قد انتهينا في دراساتنا السابقة إلى اليقين التام بوجود الله تعالى يقيناً يستند إلى مختلف الأدلة العلمية القاطعة ، وإلى اليقين ببعثة الأنبياء والرسل بما فيهم خاتم الأنبياء محمد عليه الصلاة والسلام ، وبالكتب المنزلة وحياً من الله عليهم ، كل ذلك بالأدلة المنطقية العلمية التي تم شرحها في أماكنها - فرأينا الخالق جل جلاله يقرر بأنه خلق الإنسان في أحسن تقويم ، وأنه تكاثر من نسل أبيه آدم الذي خلقه الله وبث فيه الإدراك وعلمه البيان والتعبير عن الأشياء بما ألهمه من أسمائها . ثم رأيناه يتحدث في بيانه هذا عن هؤلاء المتخاصمين حول كيفية نشأتهم والتفسير الذي يجب أن يعتمدوه لما قد تخيلوه من فرضية تطور الإنسان ، وقد أصموا آذانهم عن بيان الخالق نفسه للأمر ـ رأيناه يتحدث عنهم بأسلوب يشع بالرهبة وجلال الربوبية ، قائلاً ﴿ ما أشهدتُهم خَلْق السمواتِ والأرض ولا خَلْق أنفُسهم وما كنتُ مُتَّخِذَ المُضِلَّينَ عَضُداً ﴾ [ الكهف : ٥١ ] . هكذا بحثنا واستقصينا . فبأي الاحتمالات نؤمن ونصدق ؟ أنغمض العين والفكر ونؤمن بواحد من تلك المذاهب السالف ذكرها على ما تعانيه من ثغرات وترزح تحته انتقادات ونحمل العقل كرهاً على افتراضه ثم التصديق بـه . أم من نؤمن بتقرير الخالق نفسه بعد أن آمنا به وفرغنا من الإيمان برسله وكتبه وقرآنه ؟ لا يتردد العاقل الحر لحظة واحدة في أن علينا - بعد إيماننا بالله ورسله وكتبه - أن نطرح اضطراب المضطربين وحيرة المحتارين جانباً . ثم نصدق الخبر الصادق الثابت الواصل إلينا بطريق القطع والتواتر . نقول هذا كله عن قصة خلق الإنسان التي ورد شرحها في كلام الله عز وجل بعبارة صريحة قاطعة لا تحتمل لبساً ولا تأويلاً .
Therefore, we must turn and listen to the statement of the Creator Himself, as He tells us about the detail of the matter and its reality. And we had previously concluded in our earlier studies complete certainty of the existence of God Almighty, a certainty based on various definitive scientific proofs, and certainty of the mission of the prophets and messengers including the seal of the prophets Muhammad (peace and blessings be upon him), and of the books revealed as revelation from God to them, all of that by logical scientific proofs that have been explained in their places. We saw the Creator, whose glory is great, stating that He created man in the best stature, and that he multiplied from the progeny of his father Adam, whom God created, instilled in him perception, and taught him expression and articulation of things through inspiration of their names. Then we saw Him in this statement talking about those disputants about the manner of their origin and the interpretation they must adopt for what they imagined of the hypothesis of human evolution, and they blocked their ears from the Creator's own statement of the matter — we saw Him talking about them in a style radiating with awe and the majesty of Lordship, saying: {I did not make them witness to the creation of the heavens and the earth, nor to the creation of themselves, nor would I take the misleaders as assistants} [Al-Kahf: 51]. Thus we searched and investigated. So which probabilities do we believe and accept? Do we close the eye and mind and believe in one of those previously mentioned schools, despite the gaps they suffer from and the criticisms they bear, and force the mind to assume and then believe it? Or do we believe in the statement of the Creator Himself after we have believed in Him and completed belief in His messengers, His books, and His Quran? The free rational person does not hesitate for a moment that we must — after our faith in God, His messengers, and His books — set aside the confusion of the confused and the bewilderment of the perplexed. Then we accept the truthful, confirmed report that has reached us via the method of definitiveness and tawatur (mass transmission). We say all this about the story of human creation, whose explanation has come in the speech of God Almighty in clear, decisive words that admit no ambiguity nor interpretation.
Source pages p. 269

Commentary
This passage is an argumentative exhortation. Buti begins by calling the reader to listen to the Creator's own statement about the origin of humans, contrasting it with human hypotheses. He first recaps the certainties established in previous studies: the existence of God through definitive proofs, the mission of prophets and messengers including Muhammad, and the divine revelation of books. All these are grounded in logical and scientific evidence. Then he highlights the Quranic account: God created man in the best form, and humanity multiplied from Adam, whom God endowed with perception and language. Buti then notes that the Quran itself addresses those who dispute this, rejecting their hypothesis of human evolution, and quotes verse 18:51 where God says He did not call them to witness creation. After this, Buti poses a rhetorical question: which do we believe? The flawed human schools that require us to force our minds to accept them despite their gaps, or the Creator's own statement after we have already believed in Him, His messengers, and His books? He answers decisively: a free rational person does not hesitate. After faith in God, prophets, and scriptures, we must set aside all confusion and accept the true, confirmed report that reaches us through definitive transmission (tawatur). He concludes that the Quranic account of human creation is explicit, decisive, and admits no ambiguity or interpretation. The lesson thus establishes the priority of revealed truth over speculative human theories once the foundations of faith are secure.

Investigating Animal Origins: Caution and the Quranic Principle
Buti clarifies the approach to animal origins: rational investigation allowed but bound by Quranic epistemic principle.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Buti's two conditions for investigating the origins of animals and the Quranic principle that governs such inquiry.

Core Idea
Rational investigation is allowed, but only with epistemic caution and Quranic accountability.

Buti addresses a subtle question: when the Quran is silent on a matter like the origin of animals, are we free to investigate? He says yes, but with strict boundaries. This passage explains two conditions that prevent unfounded speculation, grounded in a powerful Quranic verse. Let's examine his careful reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Understand Buti's permission to investigate
Notice that Buti first grants permission: every rational person may investigate because the Quran is silent. This sets the stage.
Buti uses the phrase 'turned the page' to indicate the Quran's silence.
2
Identify the two conditions
Read Buti's two conditions: avoid baseless assumptions, and only give certainty to things with complete proofs. Then see how he ties it to the Quranic principle.
The principle from verse 17:36 creates an obligation to not pursue what you lack knowledge of.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أما الحيوانات الأخرى فإن لكل عاقل - وقد ضرب القرآن صفحاً عن قصة نشأتها - أن يبحث في الأمر إذا أحب ، على أن لا يطوح فكره بين افتراضات غيبية لا سند لها ولا شاهد عليها ، وأن لا يعطي يقينه إلا لما تكاملت عنده أدلة العلم اليقيني ، ملتزماً في ذلك المبدأ الذي ألزمنا الله تعالى به : وَلا تَقْفُ ما لَيْسَ لَكَ بِهِ عِلم ، إِنَّ السَّمعَ والبَصَرَ والفؤادَ كُلُّ أُولئِكَ كَانَ عَنْهُ مَسؤولاً .
As for other animals, every rational person — since the Quran has turned the page on the story of their origin — may investigate the matter if he wishes, provided that he does not let his thought swing among baseless assumptions that have no support nor witness, and that he does not give his certainty except to what has been completed for him by the proofs of certain knowledge, adhering in that to the principle that God Almighty has obligated us with: {And do not pursue that of which you have no knowledge. Indeed, the hearing, the sight, and the heart — all of those will be questioned about it}.
Source pages p. 270

Commentary
This passage is a methodological clarification. Buti addresses the origin of non-human animals, noting that the Quran is silent about their creation story (it 'turns the page'). Therefore, a rational person is allowed to investigate the matter if they wish. However, Buti imposes two conditions: first, one must not let his thought wander among baseless assumptions that have no evidence or witness; second, one must not give his certainty except to what has been established by complete proofs of certain knowledge. He then grounds this in a Quranic principle from verse 17:36: do not pursue what you have no knowledge of, as hearing, sight, and heart will be questioned. Thus, investigation is permitted but strictly bounded by epistemological caution and the obligation to avoid unfounded claims.

Buti permits investigation into animal origins but confines it to epistemic caution and the Quranic commandment not to pursue unfounded knowledge.

Classifying Angels as Cosmic Existents
Author defines cosmic existents vs unseen future events and classifies angels.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the methodological distinction between cosmic existents (al-kawniyyat) and unseen future events (al-ghaybiyyat), and why angels are classified under the former.

Core Idea
Angels are classified under cosmic existents, not unseen future events.

The author begins a new section on angels by clarifying a methodological point. He anticipates that readers might assume angels belong to the category of unseen things (al-ghaybiyyat), but he deliberately places them under cosmic existents (al-kawniyyat). To understand why, we must grasp his precise definitions of these two categories.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation once. Notice the author's definitions and the reasoning behind his classification.
2
Understand the definitions
Focus on the definitions of al-kawniyyat (cosmic existents) and al-ghaybiyyat (unseen future events). See how they differ in scope.
Al-kawniyyat includes all created stable existents; al-ghaybiyyat refers specifically to future events not yet occurred.
3
Apply the classification
Using the definitions, understand why angels fall under al-kawniyyat. They are already created and existent, unlike future events.
The author also notes that existents are broader than what is witnessed.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثانيا
الملائكة:
وإنما جعلنا الحديث عن الملائكة والجن ، في قسم الكونيات ، مع ما قد يخطر في البال ، من أنهم إنما يدخلون في الغيبيات التي لا نشاهدها ولا نعلم عنها إلا ما أخبر به الكتاب من شأنها - لأنا نقصد بالكونيات جميع ما هو مكون أي موجود ثابت . ونقصد بالغيبيات جميع ما أخبر الله عن وقوعه مما لم يقع بعـد ، وقوعاً كلياً . والملائكة يدخلون ، بهذا المعنى ، في الصنف الأول . فهم مخلوقون يتصفون بالكينونة والوجود ، كالجن ، وقد رأى بعضهم الأنبياء عليهم صلوات الله وسلامه ، ولا يُشكل في الموضوع أن عامة الناس لا يرونهم . فقد علمت مما ذكرناه آنفاً أن الموجودات أعم من المشاهدات
Secondly, the angels: We have placed the discussion of angels and jinn in the section of cosmic existents (al-kawniyyat), despite what may come to mind that they are part of the unseen things (al-ghaybiyyat) which we do not witness and know only through what the Book has informed about them – because we mean by cosmic existents (al-kawniyyat) all that is composed, i.e., an existent that is stable (thābit). And we mean by unseen things (al-ghaybiyyat) all that God has informed of its occurrence, which has not yet occurred, in a comprehensive occurrence. And the angels, in this sense, enter into the first category. For they are created beings characterized by beingness and existence, like the jinn, and some of them have been seen by the prophets – peace and blessings of God be upon them – and it is not problematic in the subject that common people do not see them. For you have known from what we mentioned earlier that existents are more general than witnessed things.
Source pages p. 273

Commentary
This passage is a methodological clarification. The author begins by stating that he has placed the discussion of angels and jinn under the section of cosmic existents (al-kawniyyat). He anticipates an objection: one might think angels belong to the unseen (al-ghaybiyyat) because we do not see them and only know them through revelation. To resolve this, he defines his terms precisely. 'Cosmic existents' (al-kawniyyat) means everything that is composed or created and exists in a stable manner. 'Unseen future events' (al-ghaybiyyat) means matters that God has informed will happen in the future but have not yet occurred as a whole. Angels, being already created and existing, fall into the first category. They are created beings like jinn. While most people do not see them, some prophets have seen them. The author concludes by reiterating the logical point: existents are more general than what is witnessed, so not being seen does not negate existence.

الغيبيات
مكون
موجود
كينونة

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Angels are unseen, so they must be part of al-ghaybiyyat (unseen things).
Correction: Al-ghaybiyyat in this context specifically refers to future events that have not yet occurred, not all unseen things. Angels are already created and exist, so they are cosmic existents.

Checkpoint

C) Because the Quran mentions them in the section on creation

Key Takeaway

Ignorance Does Not Prove Non-Existence
Al-Buti states the epistemological principle that ignorance is not evidence for absence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that the absence of evidence for something's existence is not evidence of its non-existence, and that ignorance is a state of the knower, not a property of the known.

Core Idea
Lack of proof for existence is not proof of non-existence.

In this passage, al-Buti corrects a common logical fallacy: confusing ignorance with evidence. He reminds us that believing something does not exist requires just as much proof as believing it does. This short but powerful principle is foundational for sound reasoning about unseen realities.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice that al-Buti uses a conditional structure to make his point.
2
Identify the two sides of belief
Al-Buti says that both belief in existence and belief in non-existence require scientific proof. Find these two statements in the text.
This is the core of the principle.
3
Understand the definition of ignorance
He defines ignorance as the state when no proof exists for either side. He emphasizes that ignorance is a quality of the person, not of the thing under investigation.
This is a key insight: ignorance tells you about yourself, not about the thing.
4
Consider the consequence
Al-Buti concludes that if decisive proof later appears, it is futile to cling to one's prior ignorance. Reflect on why this is logically necessary.
This prevents using ignorance as a permanent argument.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويغيب عن ذهن بعض البسطاء من الناس أنه كما لا يجوز الإيمان بوجود الشيء إلا إذا ثبت الدليل العلمي على وجوده فإنه لا يجوز أيضاً الإيمان بفقدان الشيء إلا إذا ثبت الدليل العلمي على فقدانه . فإذا لم يثبت الدليل العلمي لا على الوجود ولا على العدم، فتلك هي الحالة التي يسمى الإنسان فيها جاهلاً . وجهلك بالشيء لا يستلزم فقده ولا وجوده ، إذ هو صفة متلبسة بك ، لا بالشيء المبحوث عنه . ذلك الشيء أو [؟] فإذا ظهر لك برهان علمي قاطع يجزم بأحد طرفي وجود عدمه ، فإن من العبث أن تقارع ذلك البرهان القاطع بجهلك السابق .
And it escapes the mind of some simple people that just as it is not permissible to believe in the existence of a thing unless scientific proof for its existence is established, it is also not permissible to believe in the absence of a thing unless scientific proof for its absence is established. So if neither proof for existence nor for absence is established, that is the state in which a person is called ignorant. And your ignorance of a thing does not entail its absence nor its existence, for it is a quality attached to you, not to the thing under investigation. That thing or [؟]. Then if a decisive scientific proof appears to you that affirms one of the two sides—existence or non-existence—then it is futile to counter that decisive proof with your previous ignorance.
Source pages p. 282

Commentary
This passage states an epistemological principle about belief and evidence. Al-Buti begins by noting a common error among simple people: they think that belief in something requires proof, but they forget that disbelief (belief in absence) also requires proof. He clarifies that ignorance—the lack of evidence either way—is a state of the knower, not a property of the thing itself. If no proof exists for existence or absence, one remains ignorant; ignorance alone does not justify denial. The passage ends with a conditional: if decisive proof later appears, it is absurd ('عبث') to cling to one's prior ignorance as an argument.

Key Terms
جهل (ignorance)
دليل علمي (scientific proof)
وجود (existence)
عدم (non-existence)
برهان قاطع (decisive proof)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That lacking proof for something's existence is itself proof of its non-existence.
Correction: Al-Buti clarifies that ignorance—lack of proof—is a state of the knower, not evidence about the thing. Both existence and non-existence require separate proof.

Checkpoint
According to al-Buti, what is the proper stance when there is no scientific proof for either the existence or non-existence of something?
A) Deny its existence.
B) Affirm its existence.
C) Acknowledge ignorance.
D) Claim it is impossible.

Key Takeaway
Ignorance alone is not a valid basis for denying the existence of something.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever dismissed a truth about your own shortcomings because you lacked evidence from your own experience? Think of a time when your ignorance of a problem allowed you to deny its existence. What would it take for you to accept decisive proof?
?
When you encounter a religious command or prohibition that you don't understand, does your lack of understanding lead you to doubt its validity? How will you respond the next time such a command appears to be without evidence in your personal experience?
?
In your journey of faith, have you ever clung to your ignorance as an excuse not to act? What if decisive proof has already appeared to you? Will you let your past ignorance prevent you from embracing the truth when it is clear?

Critique of Contradictory Attitudes Toward Proof
Buti criticizes a person who rejects scientific proof but accepts baseless Western claims.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the logical inconsistency of rejecting scientific proof while uncritically accepting baseless claims, and the importance of intellectual independence.

Core Idea
Blind rejection of evidence is no better than blind acceptance of claims.

Buti draws attention to a troubling contradiction: a person who claims to champion science yet dismisses scientific proof, while meekly accepting hollow Western assertions. This lesson unpacks his critique and the powerful Arab proverb he uses to expose this absurdity.

Guided Path
1

The passage describes two scenarios: how the person reacts to scientific proof (denial) and to empty Western claims (submission). Mark these in the text.

The Arab proverb 'You are in the water, yet your head is in the sky' is used to illustrate obliviousness. Reflect on how it applies to the person's situation.
The footnote explains the proverb meaning.

Buti questions the value of a science that doesn't grant independent thought. Discuss why intellectual independence is essential for genuine scientific inquiry.

That appearance!.. It is the absurdity that cannot be represented in anything lower or uglier than this. Someone presents himself boastfully to you as a denier, in the name of science and the evidence of science, when you place him before the scientific proof according to its precise intellectual method. Then you see him shrinking in humiliation and twisting his head in broken submission and blind faith, when you place him before empty claims of some Western thinkers or their orientalists. What kind of science is this that wobbles in his brain and brags while it has not yet earned him even the independent personality that makes him able to think with his own mind? May Allah have mercy on that Arab who knew the root of the disease in this and its likes, the day he said: 'You are in the water, and your head is in the sky!'.. (1) It is an Arab proverb used for one who boasts of what he is not worthy of.

Commentary
This passage is a critique. The author begins by calling the attitude 'sakhāfah' (absurdity), saying nothing is lower or uglier. He describes a person who, when confronted with scientific proof, denies it boastfully in the name of science. But when faced with empty claims of Western thinkers, he submits humbly. The author questions the value of such a science that does not give him independence of thought. He then cites an Arab proverb: 'You are in the water, yet your head is in the sky,' symbolizing someone oblivious to obvious truth. The footnote explains the proverb. The author uses this to highlight the contradiction and lack of critical thinking.

Methodological Justification for Discussing the Proof of Angels and Jinn
Buti explains why he expounded on the proof of angels and jinn.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Buti expanded on the proof of angels and jinn as a methodological foundation for all discussions of the unseen.

Core Idea
The attitude toward angels's existence sets the pattern for all unseen matters.

In the previous sections, Buti engaged deeply with the scientific proof for angels and jinn. Here he pauses to explain his method: that this discussion is not a digression but a template. The same logic of proof—and the same pitfalls of simplistic rejection or acceptance—will reappear for every unseen matter. Understanding why he labored this point helps us read his entire project correctly.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage and English translation side by side. Notice the phrase 'في سلبه وإيجابه' (in negation and affirmation). This signals that the proof method applies both to proving and disproving claims about the unseen.
2
Identify the author's stated reason
The author says he expanded the discussion because 'it is the same attitude that these people adopt towards the unseen matters'. Why would that justify expansion? Ponder the pedagogical logic.
3
Connect to broader methodology
Consider how this passage functions as a signpost. Buti is training the reader's mind to handle all ghaybiyyat (unseen matters) with a consistent rational method. This lesson is about method, not content.

He states he wanted to expand the topic to apply its logic (both affirmative and negative) to subsequent discussions. This shows the importance of establishing a correct methodology for dealing with the unseen.

Author concludes and links to future unseen matters.

No Religious Danger in Scientific Exploration of the Cosmos
Argues that Islamic teachings do not forbid cosmic exploration; it falls under 'taskhir'.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Islamic teachings do not prohibit cosmic exploration and how the Quranic concept of taskhir actually encourages it.

Core Idea
The Quran's concept of subjugation invites cosmic exploration.

Some assume that Islam discourages scientific exploration beyond Earth, but the Quranic concept of 'taskhir' suggests otherwise. In this passage, the author clarifies that there is no religious barrier to discovering cosmic realities through thought and observation. Let's examine the reasoning and see how the word 'taskhir' itself supports such endeavors.

Guided Path
1
Understand the claim
The passage starts with a premise: if you have grasped the truth (from previous context), then know there is no religious danger. Recognize the author's response to a misunderstanding.
The 'truth' refers to earlier discussions about divine transcendence and causality.
2
Identify the three 'no religious impediment' statements
The author lists three things that are not prohibited: rising through reflection to knowledge of cosmic realities, discovering them through observation (including space travel), and believing reports of such events. Note the emphasis on 'by sense and observation'.
3
Connect to the Quranic concept of taskhir
The author asserts that all these activities fall under the Quran's meaning of 'taskhir' (subjugation). See how the word itself implies that humans can probe cosmic truths using intellect, observation, and touch.
Taskhir is often used for subjugation of natural phenomena for human benefit.
4
Consider the implication
If taskhir were limited, then the word would not carry its full meaning. So the Quranic concept actually encourages exploration. Reflect on how this aligns with scientific inquiry.
This connects to the broader theme of Islam and science.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإذا أدركت هذه الحقيقة، فاعلم أنه لا يوجد أي خطر ديني كما قد يتوهم بعض الجهال من أن يرتقي الإنسان بالتأمل والفكر إلى معرفة الكثير من حقائق الكون المختلفة من حوله قريباً كان أو بعيداً. كما لا يوجد أي مانع ديني من أن يتوصل بعد ذلك إلى اكتشاف هذه الحقائق بالحس والمشاهدة، كاجتياز طبقات الجو واكتشاف الكواكب القريبة أو البعيدة عن كتب، بل والصعود إليها والإقامة فيها إن أمكن ذلك. كما لا يوجد أي مانع من أن يصدق المسلم نبأ حدوث شيء من هذه الأمور. إذ إن هذا كله إنما يدخل ضمن معنى ( التسخير ( الذي عبر به القرآن. بل إن هذه الكلمة لتنطق ببين القول، بأن الإنسان يستطيع إن هو أعمل كامل عقله وتفكيره - أن يسبر أغوار كثير من الحقائق الكونية وأن يهتدي إليها بالفكر والمشاهدة واللمس، وإلا لم تكن كلمة التسخير جارية على حقيقتها ولا متضمنة كامل معناها.
So if you have grasped this truth, then know that there is no religious danger—as some ignorant people may suppose—in man rising, through reflection and thought, to knowledge of many different realities of the universe around him, near or far. Likewise, there is no religious impediment to his subsequently arriving at the discovery of these realities through sense and observation, such as traversing the layers of the atmosphere and discovering the planets near or far, absolutely, and even ascending to them and residing in them if possible. Likewise, there is no impediment to a Muslim believing a report of the occurrence of any of these things. For all of this comes within the meaning of 'subjugation' (taskhir) that the Quran has expressed. Rather, this word unequivocally implies that man—if he employs his full intellect and thinking—can probe the depths of many cosmic realities and be guided to them through thought, observation, and touch; otherwise, the word 'taskhir' would not be applied in its true sense nor would it contain its full meaning.
Source pages p. 297

Commentary
This passage addresses a misconception: that Islamic teachings forbid human exploration of the cosmos. The author argues that there is no religious danger (khatar dini) in humans advancing through reflection to understand the universe, nor any religious barrier to discovering these realities through empirical observation, including space travel and colonization. A Muslim may even believe reports of such events. All of this falls under the Quranic concept of taskhir (subjugation). The word itself indicates that man, by fully using his intellect and thinking, can explore and understand cosmic truths through thought, observation, and even physical contact. If this were not possible, the word taskhir would not carry its true meaning. Thus, the Quranic concept of subjugation actually encourages scientific exploration.

Key Terms
تسخير
خطر ديني
مانع ديني

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some people think that Islam forbids space exploration and scientific investigation of the cosmos.
Correction: The passage clarifies that there is no religious impediment; in fact, the Quranic concept of taskhir implies that humans are meant to probe cosmic realities using intellect and observation.

Checkpoint

B) Because it falls under the meaning of 'taskhir' in the Quran.
C) Because the Prophet encouraged it.
D) Because it is a modern necessity.

Key Takeaway
The Quranic concept of taskhir encourages humans to explore the cosmos using intellect, observation, and touch.
